(۱۰) مدرسہ نظاہر العلوم سہارن پور، خانقاہ امدادیہ تھانہ بھون، دیوبندی دہلی کے مفتیان کرام اور دیگر اکابر علما ہند کی جو تصدیقات قدیم نسخے میں آغاز کتاب میں شامل تھیں ان کو آخر کتاب میں شریک اشاعت کیا گیا ۔ مذکورہ تمام امور کی انجام دہی میں غیر معمولی احتیاط سے کام لیا گیا، پھر بھی سهو و نسیان خارج از امکان نہیں۔ اس لیے جو سہو نظر سے گزرے از راه نوازش راقم الحروف کو مطلع فرمائیں تا کہ آئندہ اس کی اصلاح
کی جاسکے۔
20. (9) Detailed discussion of marriage and the rulings of prohibition by marriage (musaharat), discussion of kufu (equality in marriage) and marriage with a non-kufu have been presented. And in the treatise Hukm al-Izdawaj, the rulings of marriage with non-Muslim nations and European nations have been stated. And like the previous edition, in Risala al-Marqumat lil-Mazlumat, a general summary of all the mentioned treatises has been presented. Also, in Rafaq al-Mujtahidin, comprehensive answers have been presented to the questions raised on Hila Najiza and the doubts cast on Hila Najiza. During the establishment of the Department of Judiciary and Shariah Court (Dar al-Qada) at the mother institution Darul Ulum Deoband for about six years, the writer had the opportunity to serve as the trusted representative of Dar al-Qada, and various types of Shariah cases came before him. In the light of these experiences, guidance regarding the content of notice to the plaintiff/defendant, the content of power of attorney (mukhtar nama) and third-party appointment (salis nama), and preparing the official status of a Shariah case, including drafts of plaint and petition, etc., have also been included in this publication. (10) The certifications of the senior scholars of Madrasa Nazahir al-Ulum Saharanpur, Khanqah Imdadiya Thana Bhawan, Deobandi Delhi, and other great scholars of India, which were included in the beginning of the book in the old edition, have now been included at the end of the book. Utmost caution has been exercised in all these matters, yet errors and omissions are not impossible. Therefore, any error that may be noticed, please kindly inform the writer so that it may be corrected in the future.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the author's afterword, listing the new additions and revisions in the current edition of Al-Hilatul Najizah. The author, Khurshid Hasan Qasmi, explains that he has included detailed discussions on marriage (nikah), the rulings on prohibition by marriage (musaharat), and the issue of kafa'ah (equality in marriage). He also mentions a special treatise on marriage with non-Muslims and Europeans (Risala Hukm al-Izdawaj). Additionally, a summary of all previous treatises (Risala al-Marqumat lil-Mazlumat) is included, and comprehensive responses to doubts and questions about Hila Najiza have been added (Rafaq al-Mujtahidin). The author draws on his practical experience as a trusted representative of the Shariah court at Darul Ulum Deoband, providing sample drafts for legal documents such as notices, powers of attorney, and plaints. He also notes that the endorsements from various scholars, previously at the beginning, are now placed at the end. He apologizes for any potential errors and requests readers to inform him for correction. This is purely descriptive front matter, not a legal ruling.

A comprehensive iftaa collection combines theoretical fiqh, contemporary treatises, practical procedural documents, and scholarly endorsements, reflecting the author's experience and attention to utility.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Scholarly Endorsements (Tasdiq) in Hanafi Iftaa Literature
Front matter: copyright assignment and list of endorsing scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of tasdiq (scholarly certification) in Hanafi iftaa works and explain how it contributes to the authority of a text.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements (tasdiq) certify that a work’s content aligns with the Hanafi tradition and is reliable for fatwa.

This passage from the front matter of Al-Hilatun Najizah lists senior scholars who certified the book. In the Hanafi tradition, such endorsements are not mere formalities; they signal that the content has been reviewed and approved by recognized authorities. This is especially important for works on sensitive issues like divorce and Shariah court procedures, as muftis and judges rely on certified texts to ensure correctness within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the passage
Distinguish the copyright transfer statement (author to publisher) from the list of endorsing scholars. Note: the copyright part is a legal declaration, while the endorsement list is scholarly.
The copyright transfer is a modern legal addition; the tasdiq list is the traditional scholarly element.
2
Analyze the terminology of certification
Focus on the word 'تصديق' (tasdiq). What does it mean in this context? It is not a formal ijazah but a certification of reliability and adherence to the Hanafi school.
Tasdiq in this context implies that the seniors reviewed the work and found it consistent with the madhhab.
3
Recognize the scholars' authority
Look at the titles and positions: Shaykh al-Hadith, Grand Mufti of Pakistan, teachers at Darul Uloom Deoband. These are heavyweight scholars; their names lend significant weight to the book.
The inclusion of such scholars indicates that the work is considered authoritative within the Indian Hanafi tradition.
4
Understand the purpose in Hanafi iftaa literature
How does this list serve readers and future muftis? It assures that the book's rulings are within the madhhab and can be reliably referenced for fatwa.
Muftis often consult works with clear scholarly pedigree to avoid relying on weak or isolated opinions.

Khurshid Hasan Qasimi, son of respected Maulana Sayyid Hasan Sahib Sardam, former teacher of Tafsir and Hadith at Darul Uloom Deoband, etc., on Thursday, according to the calendar from February, the humble Khurshid Hasan Qasimi, son of respected Maulana Sayyid Hasan Sahib (teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband), has given away all rights of the book "Al-Hilatun Najizah" i.e. rulings of divorce and the system of Shariah court, to respected Qari Muhammad Rifat Sahib, owner of Maktaba Razi, Deoband, and the humble has settled the mutual matters of the book's rights. Also, the humble has permanently given the publication rights of the mentioned book to the said Qari Sahib. Now the humble will not publish this book nor will he allow anyone else to publish it. This writing has been given so that it is appropriate and useful when needed. Cheque.

Names of the esteemed scholars who certified "Al-Hilatun Najizah":
Shaykh al-Islam Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Husain Ahmad; Shaykh al-Hadith Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Zakariyya Sahib (may Allah illuminate his grave); Faqih al-Millat Hadrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Shafi Sahib, Grand Mufti of Pakistan and former president of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Asghar Husain Miyan Sahib (may Allah illuminate his grave); Shaykh al-Adab wa al-Fiqh Hadrat Maulana Muhammad I'zaz Ali Sahib; Hadrat Maulana Abdul Latif Sahib, Nazim of Madrasa Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad As'adullah Sahib, Nazim of Madrasa Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur; Hakim al-Islam Hadrat Maulana Qari Muhammad Tayyib Sahib; Hadrat Maulana Abdul Rahman Sahib, teacher at Madrasa Mazahir al-Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Abdul Sami Sahib Deobandi, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Rasul Khan Sahib, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Muhammad Mubarak Ali Sahib, Naib Muhtamim of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Mas'ud Ahmad Sahib, Naib Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Riyaduddin Sahib, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Siraj Ahmad Sahib, student at Khanqah Imdadiyya Thana Bhawan Madrasa; Hadrat Maulana Abdul Karim Sahib Gambthlawi; and Hadrat Maulana Zafar Ahmad Usmani Sahib, Khanqah Imdadiyya Thana Bhawan; and other senior scholars and muftis of India.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts of the front matter of the book 'Al-Hilatun Najizah' by Maulana Khurshid Hasan Qasimi. The first part is a formal copyright transfer statement: the author, Khurshid Hasan Qasimi, son of Maulana Sayyid Hasan (teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband), declares that he has transferred all rights of the book—pertaining to rulings on divorce and the Shariah court system—to Qari Muhammad Rifat Sahib, owner of Maktaba Razi, Deoband. The author also states he has permanently transferred publication rights and will neither publish nor authorize others to publish the book. This is a legally binding declaration to ensure clarity and future reference. The second part lists the names of senior scholars who certified and endorsed the book, including Shaykh al-Hadith Maulana Muhammad Zakariyya, Mufti Muhammad Shafi, Hakim al-Islam Qari Muhammad Tayyib, and many others. This list signifies the scholarly authority and acceptance of the work within the Indian Hanafi tradition. The presence of these endorsements indicates that the book's content, particularly on divorce and Shariah court procedures, was reviewed and approved by leading authorities of the time.

Key Terms
حقوق (huqooq): Legal rights, specifically copyright and publication rights of the book.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Certification or endorsement by senior scholars of the book's content and reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of the list of scholars in this passage?
A) To show who contributed to writing the book
B) To certify that the book's content is reliable and within the Hanafi school
C) To grant the reader permission to teach the book
D) To indicate that the book is the official position of Darul Uloom Deoband

Key Takeaway
Scholarly endorsements (tasdiq) in the front matter of a Hanafi iftaa work serve to certify the book's reliability, but they do not replace the mufti's duty to verify rulings against the established hierarchy of evidence.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Role of Scholarly Endorsements (Tasdiq) in Hanafi Works
Listing of scholars who certified and endorsed the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of tasdiq (certification) and ta'yid (endorsement) in Hanafi books and evaluate how a mufti uses such endorsements to assess a work's reliability.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements are a mufti's shorthand: a book certified by Hanafi masters is considered reliable for fatwa.

The Al-Hilat al-Najijah opens with a prestigious list of scholars who certified the work. These endorsements are not mere ornamentation; they serve a crucial function in the Hanafi tradition by establishing the book's credibility. This lesson will teach you to read such lists, understand the weight of each title, and appreciate why muftis rely on endorsed texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholars
Read through the list and note the names and titles of the certifiers. Recognize that the first group includes major authorities (e.g., Shaykh al-Islam, Faqih al-Millat) and the second group includes teachers and muftis from various madrasas.
Titles like 'Shaykh al-Hadith' and 'Faqih al-Millat' indicate specialization.
2
Categorize the Endorsement Level
Distinguish between tasdiq (certification) and ta'yid (endorsement). Tasdiq implies a thorough verification of content, while ta'yid is a broader approval. Note that some scholars are listed specifically for 'tasdiq wa ta'yid'.
Not all endorsements carry the same weight; a tasdiq from a master jurist is stronger than a ta'yid from a lesser-known scholar.
3
Analyze the Institutional Affiliations
Observe the madrasas and positions mentioned (e.g., Darul Uloom Deoband, Madrasa Mazahir Uloom). These institutions are centers of Hanafi learning, and their involvement signals broad acceptance of the work.
The inclusion of multiple institutions indicates consensus among leading Hanafi circles.
4
Understand the Practical Significance for a Mufti
A mufti encountering an endorsed work knows that it has passed scholarly scrutiny. This saves time and reduces the risk of relying on an erroneous text. However, endorsements are not infallible; the mufti still checks the legal reasoning.
The list is a 'chain of trust' (isnad) for the book itself.
5
Apply to a New Situation
Imagine you are a mufti and you come across another Hanafi work with a similar endorsement list. Assess its reliability based on the names and titles. If unknown, you would investigate further.
This skill is part of 'takhrij al-fiqhi'—tracing the authority of a text.

The names of the great scholars who certified (tasdiq) al-Hilat al-Najijah: Shaykh al-Islam Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Husayn Ahmad; Shaykh al-Hadith Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Zakariyya, may Allah illuminate his grave; Faqih al-Millat Hadrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Shafi', Grand Mufti of Pakistan and former member of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Asghar Husayn Miyan, may Allah illuminate his grave; Shaykh al-Adab wa al-Fiqh Hadrat Maulana Muhammad I'zaz Ali; Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Latif, Nazim of Madrasa Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad As'ad Allah, Nazim of Madrasa Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur; Hakim al-Islam Hadrat Maulana Qari Muhammad Tayyib; Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Rahman, teacher at Madrasa Mazahir al-Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Sami' Deobandi, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Rasul Khan, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Sayyid Muhammad Mubarak Ali, Naib Muh'tamim of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Mas'ud Ahmad, Naib Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Muhammad Riyad al-Din, teacher at Darul Uloom Deoband; Hadrat Maulana Siraj Ahmad, who studied in the three Khanqahs of Imdadiyya Thana Bhawan Madrasa; Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Karim Gomathelvi; Hadrat Maulana Zafar Ahmad Uthmani, Khanqah Imdadiyya Thana Bhawan; and other great scholars and muftis of Hind. Shah, Sadr Mufti of Madrasa Aliya Imdadiyya Muradabad; Maulana Khalil Ahmad, Mufti of Madrasa Aliya Imdadiyya; Maulana Muhammad Sayyid Hasan.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is part of the front matter of 'Al-Hilat al-Najijah' by Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi. It lists two groups of scholars: first, the major 'akabir' (great scholars) who certified the book, and second, additional scholars who provided their endorsement (tasdiq wa ta'yid). Such endorsements are common in traditional Hanafi works to establish the book's reliability and adherence to the madhhab. The list includes prominent figures like Shaykh al-Islam Maulana Sayyid Husayn Ahmad Madani, Shaykh al-Hadith Maulana Muhammad Zakariyya Kandhlawi, and Mufti Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi, all towering authorities in the Hanafi tradition. The fact that these scholars verified the work indicates that it is a trustworthy reference for Hanafi fiqh, particularly on the topic of legal stratagems (hiyal). The second list includes teachers and muftis from various madrasas, further reinforcing the book's acceptance. This page has no legal rulings but serves a testimonial function.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): Certification or verification of the book's contents by a scholar, confirming its correctness and adherence to the Hanafi madhhab.
تائید (ta'yid): Endorsement or support for the work, indicating the scholar approves of its content and methodology.
أكابر (akabir): Great scholars, often referring to senior authorities in a specific tradition or institution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Taqriz in Hanafi Scholarship
List of endorsing scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of scholarly endorsements (taqriz) in Hanafi works and evaluate their role in establishing a book's credibility.

Core Idea
Taqriz is a scholarly endorsement that adds weight, not a chain of transmission.

This lesson examines the list of scholars who verified Al-Hilatul Najijah. While not a legal passage, this front matter reflects an important aspect of Hanafi scholarly tradition: the practice of seeking and displaying endorsements from contemporaries to strengthen a work's authority. Understanding this context helps a mufti assess the reliability of sources and the etiquette of scholarly verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type
Recognise that this is front matter (taqriz list), not a legal ruling. The names and affiliations are endorsements, not an isnad.
Taqriz differs from ijazah (license) or sanad (chain).
2
Analyse the function of taqriz
Understand that taqriz serves to establish the book's acceptability among contemporary scholars, encouraging wider acceptance and use.
In Hanafi works, taqriz often appears in later publications, especially from the Indian subcontinent.
3
Connect to adab al-mufti
Consider how a mufti should view such endorsements: they indicate scholarly approval but do not override textual evidence. A mufti still evaluates the book's content independently.
Taqriz is a sign of credibility, not a substitute for critical analysis.
4
Apply to modern context
Reflect on how a mufti today might use endorsements from trusted 'ulama when recommending a fatwa collection to the community.
The same principle applies: endorsements from reputable scholars add weight but are not binding proof.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Need for Legal Stratagems (Hiyal): The Author's First Reason
Author states the first reason for compiling the collection of legal stratagems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first reason for compiling Al-Hilatul Najijah and explain how the absence of a shari qadi necessitates recourse to alternative legal opinions (hiyal) within the Hanafi and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
When the ideal Islamic judiciary is absent, hiyal (legal stratagems) become necessary to prevent greater harm like apostasy.

In this passage from the preface of Al-Hilatul Najijah, Ashraf Ali Thanwi explains his motivation for compiling a collection of legal stratagems. He addresses a pressing problem: Muslim women in British India suffering from oppressive husbands with no access to a shari qadi. Without relief, some women are driven to apostasy. The author's response is to compile a resource drawing from both Hanafi and Maliki schools to provide practical solutions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
Read the opening of the passage to find the first reason given for compiling the book. Look for key phrases about 'answering objections' and 'women's hardships'.
The author explicitly says the first reason is to respond to objections related to women's sufferings from their husbands.
2
List the husband's defaults mentioned
The author enumerates several husband-related problems that cause women distress: impotence, insanity, epilepsy, failure to provide maintenance despite wealth, etc. List them from the text.
These are the practical problems that drive the need for legal stratagems.
3
Note the absence of a shari qadi
The author highlights that in India there is no shari qadi (Islamic judge) to provide relief. This absence is a key factor leading women to consider apostasy.
The lack of a formal Islamic judicial system creates a vacuum that hiyal are meant to fill.
4
Understand the consequence: apostasy
The author reports that many women, distressed by their husbands' oppression and unable to obtain a divorce legally, resort to apostasy to dissolve the marriage. This is the urgent problem the book aims to prevent.
Apostasy is a serious religious and social harm; the author's collection of hiyal is designed to offer lawful alternatives.

بسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحمٰنِ الرَّحِيمِ
تالیف کتاب کی پہلی وجہ
حمد و صلواۃ کے بعد عرض ہے کہ یہ رسالہ چند مادری[؟] کا مجموعہ ہے جن میں تقویمین[؟] طلاق منکوحہ کا مسلہ ہے یعنی نکاح کے وقت بیوی کو حق طابق[؟] سپرد کر دینے کا مسئلہ ہے تو جو رسالہ پہلا جزو ہے اس میں حنفیہ کے مذہب کے مطابق فتوی ہے اور اس کے دوسرے جزو میں مذہب مالکیہ مدینہ منورہ کے مفتیان کرام ہیں جن میں سے بعض اجزاء فقہ حنفی میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں اور بعض ابتزامہ[؟] مذہب مالکیہ کی فقہ کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ اور ان رسائل کو جمع کرنے کی دو وجہ میں پہلی وجہ تو ان اعتراضات کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے جو کہ عورتوں کی تکالیف سے تعلق ہیں جن کا تعلق شوہر سے ہے جس کے مندرجہ ذیل اسباب ہیں۔
شوہر کا کم ہوتا[؟]، مجنون ہونا، سنین[؟]، نامرد ہونا، دوست[؟] کے باوجود ہوئی کو نان و نفقه نه دیتا در غیره و غیره
بیوی کے مرتد ہونے سے نکاح فتح[؟] ہوگا انا وزوجہ سے کا فن[؟] نہیں ہوتا؟ و بعض لقوں[؟] کی جانب سے اعتراض ہے کہ اسلام شرعی قاضی کے بغیر براہ راست خواتین کو مصائب (مذکورہ) سے نجات کا کوئی طریقہ تجویز نہیں کیا جبکہ ہندوستان میں شرعی قاضی کا وجود نہیں، بہر حال شوہر کے مذکورہ مظالم سے تنگ آکر بہت سی خواتین مرتد ہو جاتی ہیں چنانچہ کچھ ہی دن پہلے سنا تھا کہ بعض علاقوں میں بہت کم وقفہ میں کافی تعداد میں عورتیں مرتد ہو
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The first reason for composing the book. After praise and salutations, it is stated that this treatise is a collection of several articles which include the issue of dividing [the rights] of the married woman's divorce, i.e., the issue of entrusting the right of khula to the wife at the time of marriage. So the treatise which is the first part contains a fatwa according to the Hanafi school, and in its second part are the noble muftis of Medina of the Maliki school, some parts of which are also found in Hanafi fiqh, and some are specific to the fiqh of the Maliki school. And among the two reasons for compiling these treatises, the first reason is intended to answer those objections that are related to women's hardships which are connected to the husband, for which the following causes exist: the husband being impotent, insane, epileptic, impotent, not providing maintenance despite having wealth, etc. And from the apostasy of the wife, the marriage will dissolve? Is it not an art from the wife? And some people object that Islam has not prescribed any direct way for women to gain relief from the aforementioned afflictions without a shari qadi, while in India there is no shari qadi. Nevertheless, many women, distressed by the aforementioned oppressions of the husband, become apostates. Thus, just a few days ago, I heard that in some areas, within a very short period, a considerable number of women had apostatized.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the author's preface explaining the first reason for compiling the book. The author states that the book is a collection of treatises addressing issues related to divorce and khula (the wife's right to seek dissolution). Some parts follow the Hanafi school, while others follow the Maliki school, as practiced by the muftis of Medina. The first reason for compilation is to respond to objections raised regarding the difficulties women face from their husbands, such as impotence, insanity, epilepsy, failure to provide maintenance, etc. The author notes a particular objection: that Islam does not provide a direct remedy for women without a shari qadi, who is absent in India. This leads some women to apostatize, which the author highlights with a recent anecdote of mass apostasy in some regions.

Key Terms
حیلہ شرعیہ (hīlah shar‘iyyah): A legal stratagem that conforms to the Shari'ah, used to achieve a permissible end by using a different legal mechanism or school.
قاضی شرعی (qāḍī shar‘ī): A judge appointed by an Islamic state to adjudicate disputes according to Shari'ah.
افتیاء (iftā’): The act of issuing a fatwa (legal opinion) on a matter of Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The absence of a shari qadi necessitates the use of hiyal (legal stratagems) from other schools to prevent greater harm such as apostasy.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Establishing a Shari'a Judiciary and the Answer to Objections on Women's Hardships
Defending Islam against the objection of lacking a Shari'a judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the objection against Islam regarding women's hardships without a Shari'a judge, and construct the Hanafi response based on responsibility and the need for a qualified judiciary.

Core Idea
Islam provides the cure; Muslims must administer it.

In this passage, Ashraf Ali Thanwi addresses a critical objection raised against Islamic law in British India: that Islam does not provide a direct solution for women suffering from oppressive husbands because a Shari'a judge is absent. The author defends Islam by clarifying that the Shari'a does prescribe a mechanism—through appointed judges—but the obligation to implement it falls upon the Muslim community. This lesson unpacks the author's argument, focusing on the distinction between divine guidance and human responsibility, and the imperative to establish a qualified judiciary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the passage and locate the specific complaint against Islam. The objectors claim that Islam offers no escape for women from husbands who are missing, insane, sick, impotent, or withholding maintenance, because there is no Shari'a judge to annul the marriage or grant relief.
The objection is based on the absence of a qadi, not on the Shari'a ruling itself.
2
List the causes of women's hardships
The author enumerates several scenarios: husband missing (mafqud), insane (majnoon), sick (saqeem), impotent (namard), or not providing maintenance despite ability. These situations, under Hanafi law, could lead to faskh (dissolution) via a qadi, but without one, women suffer.
These are classic grounds for judicial divorce in Hanafi fiqh if a qadi could adjudicate.
3
Understand the author's response
The author argues that Islam's role is to show the path (tadbeer batlana). If Muslims do not act, the fault is on them, not on Islam. He uses the Qur'anic principle 'No bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' (6:164) to emphasize individual responsibility.
This is a key defense of the Shari'a against accusations of incompleteness.
4
Note the proposed solution
The author suggests that Muslims should strive to appoint Shari'a-compliant judges, either through government authority or by demanding such appointments. If that fails, patience (insaat) is advised, but the blame remains on Muslims.
The solution is practical: establish an Islamic judiciary, not abandon the Shari'a.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
The argument rests on the principle that Islam provides divine guidance, but implementation requires community effort. This is a recurring theme in Hanafi usul al-ifta: the mufti's fatwa is only as effective as the community's ability to enforce it.
This lesson prepares you for later discussions on the conditions of a qadi and giving fatwa according to another school.

Source Text

حمد و صلواۃ کے بعد عرض ہے کہ یہ رسالہ چند مذاہب کا مجموعہ ہے جن میں تقییم [؟] طلاق منکوحہ کا مسئلہ ہے یعنی نکاح کے وقت بیوی کو حق طلاق سپرد کر دینے کا مسئلہ ہے تو جو رسالہ پہلا جزو ہے اس میں حنفیہ کے مذہب کے مطابق فتوی ہے اور اس کے دوسرے جزء میں مذہب مالکیہ مدینہ منورہ کے مفتیان کرام ہیں جن میں سے بعض اجزاء فقہ حنفی میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں اور بعض اتباع مذہب مالکیہ کی فقہ کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ اور ان رسائل کو جمع کرنے کی دو وجہ میں پہلی وجہ تو ان اعتراضات کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے جو کہ عورتوں کی تکالیف سے تعلق ہیں جن کا تعلق شوہر سے ہے جس کے مندرجہ ذیل اسباب ہیں۔
شوہر کا مفقود ہونا، مجنون ہونا، سقیم، نامرد ہونا، دوست کے باوجود ہوئی کو نان و نفقہ نہ دیتا در غیره و غیره
بیوی کے مرتد ہونے سے نکاح فسخ ہوگا ان سے زوجہ کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہوتا؟ و بعض لقوں کی جانب سے اعتراض ہے کہ اسلام شرعی قاضی کے بغیر براہ راست خواتین کو مصائب (مذکورہ) سے نجات کا کوئی طریقہ تجویز نہیں کیا جبکہ ہندوستان میں شرعی قاضی کا وجود نہیں، بہر حال شوہر کے مذکورہ مظالم سے تنگ آکر بہت سی خواتین مرتد ہو جاتی ہیں چنانچہ کچھ ہی دن پہلے سنا تھا کہ بعض علاقوں میں بہت کم وقفہ میں کافی تعداد میں عورتیں مرتد ہو چکی ہیں اس بات کا جواب بالکل ظاہر ہے کہ اسلام کا کام صرف تدبیر بتلانا اگر مسلمان اس پر عمل نہ کریں تو قصور و الزام مسلمان ہیں، یا اسلام ؟ شرعی قاضی کے انتخاب کیلئے کوشش کی ضرورت بہر حال اس اعتراض کا اور اس مشکل کا حل یہی ہے کہ اس قسم کے حاکم اور قاضی مقرر کیے جائیں جو کہ حکومت کے اقتدار سے اس قسم کے فیصلوں کو نافذ کر سکیں اور اگر اس کی طاقت نہ ہو تو موجودہ حکومت سے مطالبہ کریں اور اس بات کی کوشش کریں کہ حکومت اس قسم کے حاکم مقرر کردے کہ جن میں وہ تمام صفات ہوں جو کہ شرعی قاضی میں ہونی چاہئیں یا کم از کم ہر ایک ضلع میں ایک اس قسم کا حاکم مقرر کیا جائے جو کہ اس قسم کے معاملات میں اختیار رکھے اگر وہ حاکم عالم نہ ہو تو قانونی طور پر اس بات کی پابندی کی جائے کہ ہر ایک معاملہ میں علماء سے فتویٰ حاصل کرے اگر کسی وجہ سے مسلمان اس بات کا انتظام نہ کریں یا ان کی اس قسم کی درخواست اور کوشش کامیاب نہ ہو تو انصات کرنا چاہیے یعنی اگر شرعی قاضی کا انتخاب نہ ہو سکے تو اس میں مسلمانوں کا قصور ہے یا اسلام کا ؟ بہ صورت مذکورہ اعتراض خود مسلمانوں پر آتا ہے نہ کہ اسلام پر، اور اسی صورت میں اسلام پر اعتراض کرنا آیت کریمہ ولا تزر وازرة وزر اخرى کے مخالف ہے۔ اور فارسی کے اس شعر کا مصداق ہے۔
نوٹ: قدیم نسخہ میں اس جگہ نہایت طویل حاشیہ تھا جس کو افادہ عام کی غرض سے آئندہ صفحات میں مسلمان عورت کا کافر سے نکاح کے عنوان سے نیز قاضی کی صفات، شرائط اور دوسرے مذہب پر فتویٰ دینے کے مدد کے عنوانات سے پیش کیا گیا۔ خورشید حسن قاسمی
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The first reason for compiling the book. After praise and salutations, the presentation is that this treatise is a collection of several schools of thought which include the issue of delegation of divorce to a married woman - meaning the issue of entrusting the right of divorce to the wife at the time of marriage. So the first part of the treatise contains a fatwa according to the Hanafi school, and its second part contains the Maliki school, [taken] from the esteemed muftis of Medina, some parts of which are also found in Hanafi fiqh, and some are specific to following the Maliki school. And the two reasons for collecting these treatises: the first reason is to respond to those objections that pertain to the hardships of women, which are related to the husband, having the following causes: the husband being missing, being insane, being sick, being impotent, not providing maintenance despite having the means, etc. The marriage will be dissolved due to the wife's apostasy; she does not benefit from her husband? And some people object that Islam has not prescribed any direct method for women to be saved from the mentioned afflictions without a Shari'a judge, whereas in India there is no Shari'a judge. Nevertheless, many women, tired of the mentioned oppressions of the husband, apostatize. Indeed, just a few days ago it was heard that in some areas, within a very short period, a considerable number of women have apostatized. The answer to this is absolutely clear: Islam's duty is only to show the way; if Muslims do not act upon it, the fault and blame lie on the Muslims, not on Islam? The need to strive for the selection of a Shari'a judge. In any case, the solution to this objection and this difficulty is that such rulers and judges should be appointed who can enforce such decisions through the authority of the government. And if that is not possible, then demand from the current government and strive for the government to appoint such rulers who possess all the qualities required of a Shari'a judge, or at least in every district such a ruler should be appointed who has authority in such matters; if that ruler is not a scholar, then legally it should be mandatory that in every case he obtains a fatwa from the scholars. If for some reason the Muslims do not arrange this, or their request and effort in this regard are unsuccessful, then they must be patient - meaning if the selection of a Shari'a judge is not possible, then the fault lies with the Muslims, not with Islam. In the mentioned manner, the objection falls upon the Muslims themselves, not upon Islam, and in this case objecting to Islam is contrary to the noble verse: 'And no bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another.' And it exemplifies this Persian verse.
Note: In the old manuscript, there was a very long footnote at this place, which, for the general benefit, is presented in the following pages under the titles: 'Marriage of a Muslim woman with a non-Muslim', 'Qualities of a judge', 'Conditions', and 'Giving fatwa according to another school'. (Khurshid Hasan Qasimi)
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the book, presenting the author's motivation for compiling this collection. The author is Ashraf Ali Thanwi, a prominent Hanafi scholar. He states that the treatise consists of legal rulings from multiple schools, primarily Hanafi and Maliki, focusing on the issue of delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) to the wife. The first part gives the Hanafi fatwa, and the second part gives the Maliki position, as per the muftis of Medina. The author then explains the first reason for compiling: to respond to objections regarding women's hardships caused by husbands (e.g., missing, insane, sick, impotent, not providing maintenance). These hardships sometimes lead women to apostasy. Objectors claim that Islam does not provide a direct solution without a Shari'a judge, which is unavailable in India. The author refutes this by arguing that Islam provides the guidance (like appointing a qualified judge), and if Muslims fail to implement it, the fault lies with them, not Islam. He suggests that Muslims should strive to appoint Shari'a judges or government officials with authority. If unsuccessful, they should be patient. This argument relies on the Qur'anic principle that no one bears another's burden. The note indicates that a long footnote in the original manuscript has been moved to later pages under separate headings.

Key Terms
تقویض طلاق منکوحہ (tafwid al-talaq al-mankuhah): The delegation of the right of divorce to the wife at the time of marriage.
شرعی قاضی (shari'i qadi): A judge appointed according to Islamic law with authority to adjudicate matrimonial and other cases.
فتویٰ (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion given by a qualified mufti based on Islamic sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ashraf Ali Thanwi, what is the primary reason for the objection that Islam lacks a solution for women's hardships?
A) The Qur'an does not address marital issues.
B) The Muslim community has failed to establish Shari'a judges.
C) The Hanafi school does not permit divorce without a qadi.
D) The government prohibits Islamic courts.

Key Takeaway
Islam provides complete guidance, but the community is responsible for establishing the institutions to implement it; blame cannot be placed on the Shari'a for human inaction.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding the Structure and Endorsements of Al-Hilat al-Najijah
Describes the book's arrangement and scholarly endorsements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the arrangement of Al-Hilat al-Najijah and identify the role of scholarly endorsements in establishing a fatwa work's authority within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A fatwa work's authority rests on both its content and the endorsements of senior scholars who validate its methodology.

A fatwa compilation is only as reliable as the scholars who stand behind it. This lesson explores the front matter of Al-Hilat al-Najijah, a Hanafi manual for problematic marriage cases. You will learn how the book is structured, what issues it addresses, and why the endorsements of senior scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur are essential for its credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's major divisions
The text states the book has two main parts: the first on tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce) and the second on separation from an insane husband. Note these as separate legal topics.
These are not the only topics; the second part also includes rulings for a defiant husband (mushta'inn) and an absent but traceable husband (gha'ib ghayr mafqud).
2
Understand the categories of husbands
Three types of husbands are addressed: present but defiant, absent but not missing, and insane. Each has different legal remedies. Recognize the terminology: mushta'inn and gha'ib ghayr mafqud.
These categories are critical in Hanafi family law for determining when a wife can seek judicial separation.
3
Recognize the significance of endorsements
Eleven scholars from Darul Uloom Deoband and four from Mazahir al-Ulum Saharanpur reviewed the work thoroughly. Their endorsements, placed at the beginning, authenticate the book's methodology and rulings.
Such endorsements are a standard practice in the Hanafi tradition to assure readers of the work's reliability.
4
Note the inclusion of Maliki fatawa
The book includes Arabic fatawa from Maliki muftis of Madinah, with specific phrases labeled as 'Riwayat Ula' and 'Riwayat Thaniyya'. This shows the author's thoroughness in seeking evidence from multiple madhahib.
The original fatawa are preserved in the 'Adad al-Ulum' institution in Thana Bhawan.

ar جدید ترتیب میں فرست تصدیق کنندگان آخریں شریک اشاعت کردی گئی اور صرف ناموں کی فہرست شروع میں لگا دی گئی ۔ خورشید حسن قاسمی ۔
ے جدید نسخہ میں اردو میں مذہب حنفی پریل سے تعلق مسائل کے عنوانات بھی دیے دیئے گئے ہیں، خورشید حسن ما ہیں۔
Arrangement of the book: The arrangement of this book is that its first part contains the fatwa on tafwid al-talaq, and the second part contains the rulings on separation of the wife of an insane husband. Similarly, detailed rulings are mentioned for the husband who is present but defiant (i.e., wayward, neglectful of the wife's rights, rebellious) and the absent but not missing husband (i.e., a husband who has gone to a foreign country etc., exists somewhere but does not fulfill the legal rights of the wife). After that, the endorsement of the elders of Deoband and Saharanpur is recorded. And at the very end, all those Arabic fatawa that were obtained from the Maliki muftis of Madinah Munawwarah have been included, so that scholars may also review them, and from those Maliki fatawa, whichever phrases are used as evidence in this book are named 'Riwayat Ula' and 'Riwayat Thaniyya'. The endorsement of the elders of India: It is known that eleven persons from Deoband and four persons from Madrasa Mazahir al-Ulum Saharanpur reviewed this composition with great deliberation and gave useful advice at various places, and spent a large portion of their valuable time, so much so that these persons should be called partners in the composition. That is why the endorsements of these fifteen persons were placed at the beginning of the composition. Besides this, endorsements of other scholars were made after the booklet was published. The originals of all these Arabic fatawa that were obtained from the muftis are preserved in the 'Adad al-Ulum' in Thana Bhawan. In the new arrangement, the list of endorsers was placed at the end and only the list of names was placed at the beginning. - Khurshid Hasan Qasimi. In the new edition, Urdu titles of issues related to the Hanafi madhhab have also been added. - Khurshid Hasan.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a description of the book's structure and its scholarly endorsements. The author outlines the contents: the first part deals with tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce), the second part addresses separation from an insane husband, a husband who is present but defiant (nashiz), and a husband who is absent but not missing. After these sections, the endorsements of senior scholars from Darul Uloom Deoband and Madrasa Mazahir al-Ulum Saharanpur are recorded. Finally, the Arabic fatawa from Maliki muftis of Madinah are included. The author explains that eleven scholars from Deoband and four from Saharanpur reviewed the work thoroughly, and their endorsements are placed at the beginning. Later endorsements from other scholars were added after publication. The original fatawa are preserved in the 'Adad al-Ulum' institution in Thana Bhawan. The passage also notes that in the new edition, the list of endorsers was moved to the end, and Urdu titles for Hanafi-related issues were added. This front matter serves to authenticate the work and clarify its arrangement for readers.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife or a third party by the husband.
مشتعنت (mushtaʿinn): A husband who is present but defiant, neglectful of his wife's rights, and rebellious.
غائب غیر مفقود (ghāʾib ghayr mafqūd): A husband who is absent but his whereabouts are known (not missing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 4 from Deoband and 11 from Saharanpur
C) 15 from Deoband only
D) 10 from each institution

Key Takeaway
Al-Hilat al-Najijah's authority is established through its clear structure, the endorsements of fifteen senior Hanafi scholars, and the inclusion of Maliki fatawa for comprehensive evidence.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Mufti Adab: The Protocol for Seeking and Applying Fatwas
Mufti adab and fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the responsibilities of the mufti and the mustafti when applying a fatwa, and explain why personal interpretation of a fatwa collection is prohibited.

Core Idea
A fatwa cannot be applied without consulting a recognized mufti; the mufti must exercise careful insight, and the seeker must involve the mufti throughout.

Ashraf Ali Thanwi's introduction to Al-Hilat al-Najizah is not merely a table of contents; it is a vital lesson in fatwa protocol. The book is designed as a resource for scholars, not a DIY manual for laypeople. This passage establishes the boundary between scholarly reference and personal action: before any ruling is applied, a qualified mufti must be consulted. This lesson explores the adab (etiquette) of both the mufti and the seeker of fatwa, grounding the student in the procedural discipline of Hanafi ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Book's Purpose and Audience
Recognise that Al-Hilat al-Najizah is a specialised fatwa collection for scholars, not a lay guide. The endorsements from fifteen scholars signal its authority but also its intended readership.
The introduction explicitly warns that the simplified summary must still be understood through a scholar.
2
Extract the Two-Part Protocol
The passage divides the responsibility into two tasks for the mustafti (seeker): first, learn the issue from a renowned mufti before acting; second, involve the mufti throughout the entire process. For the mufti, the duty is to exercise extraordinary insight and attention.
This is a mutual adab – both parties have obligations.
3
Analyse the Prohibition of Self-Application
The text explicitly says: 'They should not rely solely on their own reading ability and apply an incident to this issue.' This establishes that deriving rulings from a fatwa book without a mufti is impermissible for non-mujtahids.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of taqlid – the layperson must follow a mujtahid or mufti.
4
Understand the Mufti's Required Qualities
The mufti must be 'renowned in the art of fatwa-writing, nay, accepted in fatwa-writing' and must work with 'extraordinary insight and full attention'. This sets a high bar for competence and care.
In Hanafi ifta, the mufti must be a fully qualified jurist, not merely a literate person.

Source Text

کتاب کی ترتیب اس کتاب کی ترتیب یہ ہے کہ اس کے پہلے جزو میں تفویض طلاق کا فتوی ہے اور دوسرے میں زوجہ عین زوجہ مجنون کی تفریق کے احکام ہیں اسی طرح وہ شوہر جو کہ حاضر ہو لیکن مشتعنت ہو (یعنی آوارہ ، بیوی کے حقوق سے لاپرواہ سرکش ہو) اور غائب غیر مفقود الیعنی ایسا شوہر جو کہ غیر ملک وغیرہ پر دیں چلاگیا ہو کہیں موجود ہو لیکن بیوی کے حقوق شرعیہ ادا نہ کرتا ہو) کے تفصیلی احکام مذکور ہیں ۔

ar جدید ترتیب میں فرست تصدیق کنندگان آخریں شریک اشاعت کردی گئی اور صرف ناموں کی فہرست شروع میں لگا دی گئی ۔ خورشید حسن قاسمی ۔
ے جدید نسخہ میں اردو میں مذہب حنفی پریل سے تعلق مسائل کے عنوانات بھی دیے دیئے گئے ہیں، خورشید حسن ما ہیں۔
گیا اور اصل رسالہ میں اس استدلال کی گئی روایت کا اسی عنوان سے حوالہ بھی دے دیا ہے اور اس کا نام " الحيلة الناجزه للحيلة العاجزہ " تجویز کیا گیا ہے جس کی مناسبت ہر ایک دونوں اجزاء کے ساتھ ظاہر ہے۔
مذکورہ بالا تمام مضمون علمی نوعیت کا حیلہ ناجزہ کی جامع تلخیص کا تعارف تھا اسی وجہ سے ان تمام کا خلاصہ نہایت عام فہم اور آسان عبارت میں پیش کر دیا گیا عوام کو بجائے پوری کتاب کے یہ خلاصہ دیکھ لینا اور سمجھ لینا کافی ہے یہ خلاصہ آخریں شائع شدہ ہے۔ بہر حال اس خلاصہ کو بھی کسی عالم دین سے سمجھ لینا چاہیے لیکن عالم دین کے لیے مناسب ہے کہ اس خلاصہ کو اصل رسالہ سے مقابلہ کر لیں کہ آسانی کے لیے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ اس خلاصہ کو انشاء اللہ عنقریب مستقل طور پر بھی شائع کیا جائے گا اور اس رسالہ کا نام ہے" المرقومات للمظلومات ربیعنی مظلوم عورتوں کی مشکلا کا شرعی حل) بہر حال اعتراض مذکورہ کا جواب مکمل ہوا۔
ایک ضروری ہدایت زیر نظر تصنیف میں مذکورہ مسائل پرعمل کرنے والے حضرات کے ذمہ دو قسم کے کام میں پہلا کام تو یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ پر عمل سے پہلے کسی صاحب استعداد عالم سے جو کہ اہل علم حضرات کی رائے میں فن فتوی نویسی میں شہرت یافتہ بلکہ فتوی نویسی میں تسلیم شدہ ہوں اُن سے اچھی طرح مسئلہ سمجھ لیں صرف اپنی قوتِ مطالعہ پر اعتماد کر کے کسی واقعہ کو اس مسئلہ پر منطبق نہ کریں اور مکمل کاروائی میں ان عالم یا مستند مفتی کو اس طریقہ سے شریک رکھیں کہ مسئلہ کے ہر ایک جبر اور معاملہ کے ہر ایک پہلو کے بارے میں ان کو مطلع کرتے رہیں اور ان سے شرعی حکم دریافت کرتے رہیں اور اُن مفتی یا عالم کو بھی چاہیے کہ غیر معمولی بصیرت اور خوب توجہ سے کام لیں اور جس جگہ معمولی سا بھی
The arrangement of the book is that in its first part is the fatwa on delegated divorce (tafwid al-talaq), and in the second are the rulings on separation due to a wife whose husband is insane, similarly the detailed rulings are mentioned for a husband who is present but refractory (i.e., a vagabond, careless of the wife's rights, rebellious) and a husband who is absent but not missing (i.e., a husband who has gone to a foreign land etc., is present somewhere but does not fulfill the wife's shar'i rights). After that are the attestations of the great scholars of Deoband and Saharanpur, and at the very end all those Arabic fatwas which were obtained from the esteemed muftis of the Maliki school in Medina are included, so that the people of knowledge may also view them, and among the Maliki fatwas, whichever phrases are used as evidence in this book are named 'al-riwayat al-ula' and 'al-riwayat al-thaniyah'. The attestation of the great scholars of India: Eleven scholars from Deoband and four from Madrasa Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur reviewed this work with great scrutiny, giving beneficial advice here and there, and spent a large portion of their valuable time and reviewed it Islamically with such care that these scholars should be considered co-authors. For that reason, the attestation of these fifteen scholars is included at the beginning of the original work. Besides that, after the treatise was published, attestations of other scholars were also added. All those Arabic fatwas obtained from the muftis of Medina are preserved in the original at Thana Bhawan. In the new arrangement, the list of endorsers is placed at the end as a participant in publication, and only the list of names is placed at the beginning. - Khurshid Hasan Qasimi. In the new edition, headings of issues related to the Hanafi school have also been given in Urdu. And the reference to the narration used as evidence in the original treatise is given under the same title, and it has been named 'al-Hilat al-Najizah lil-Hilat al-'Ajizah', whose suitability with both parts is apparent. The entire aforementioned content was an introduction to the comprehensive summary of Hilat al-Najizah of an academic nature. For that reason, the summary of all that is presented in very simple and easy language; for the common people, it is sufficient to see and understand this summary instead of the full book. This summary has been published recently. In any case, this summary should also be understood from a scholar of religion, but for a scholar it is appropriate to compare this summary with the original treatise for ease. It should be kept in mind that this summary will soon be published independently, Allah willing, and the name of this treatise is 'al-Marqumat li al-Mazlumat' i.e. the shar'i solution to the problems of oppressed women. In any case, the response to the mentioned objection is complete. An essential instruction: For those who act upon the issues mentioned in this work, two types of tasks are required. The first task is that before acting on an issue, they should thoroughly understand the issue from a competent scholar who, in the opinion of the people of knowledge, is renowned in the art of fatwa-writing, nay, accepted in fatwa-writing. They should not rely solely on their own reading ability and apply an incident to this issue. And in the complete process, they should involve that scholar or authoritative mufti in such a way that they keep him informed about every detail of the issue and every aspect of the matter and seek shar'i rulings from him. And that mufti or scholar should also work with extraordinary insight and full attention, and wherever even a slightest...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an editorial introduction (front matter) that outlines the structure and scholarly context of Al-Hilat al-Najizah. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, describes that the book has two main parts: the first deals with delegated divorce (tafwid al-talaq), and the second with rulings on separation when the husband is either insane, present but refractory, or absent but not fulfilling rights. Following this, the book includes endorsements from fifteen prominent scholars of Deoband and Saharanpur, who reviewed the work meticulously and are effectively co-authors. These endorsements are placed at the beginning. Additionally, Arabic fatwas from Maliki muftis in Medina are appended, with specific narrations cited under the labels 'riwayat ula' and 'riwayat thaniyah'. The passage then explains that a simplified summary has been prepared for the layperson, but it should still be reviewed with a scholar. For scholars, they should compare the summary to the original. Finally, an essential instruction is given: those who wish to act on these rulings must first consult a qualified mufti and involve them in the entire process, and the mufti must exercise careful insight. This is a clear example of mufti adab—both the seeker and the mufti have responsibilities. The passage does not present a specific ruling or legal maxim but rather clarifies the methodology and proper use of the book, ensuring that its contents are not applied haphazardly by non-specialists.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): Scholarly attestation or endorsement confirming the correctness and reliability of the work.
حیلہ ناجزہ (al-hilat al-najizah): The effective stratagem; the title of this book, referring to a shar'i solution for a helpless wife.
مفتی (mufti): A qualified jurist who issues authoritative legal responses (fatwas).
مستفتی (mustafti): The person who seeks a fatwa; the questioner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'essential instruction' in the passage, what is the first task for someone who wants to act on the rulings in Al-Hilat al-Najizah?
A) Read the summary thoroughly and decide the ruling for oneself.
B) Consult a competent scholar who is renowned in fatwa-writing and understand the issue properly.
C) Seek the endorsement of fifteen scholars before proceeding.
D) Compare the summary with the original treatise independently.

Key Takeaway
Before applying any fatwa from a book, the seeker must consult a qualified mufti and involve him throughout; the mufti must exercise extraordinary insight and care.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Value of Scholarly Consultation Across Madhahib
Biographical note on compilation and helpers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why consulting fatawa from other madhahib (specifically Maliki) is important in Hanafi fatwa practice and identify when such consultation is necessary.

Core Idea
A mufti strengthens his fatwa by consulting other schools, especially for cases where Hanafi rulings face difficulty.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's introduction to Al-Hilat al-Najijah reveals that he actively sought fatawa from Maliki scholars, not just Hanafi ones. This practice reflects the Hanafi tradition of "al-istiftah min ghayr al-madhhab" — seeking a fatwa from another school in times of necessity or difficulty. In this lesson, we explore the etiquette (adab al-mufti) of consulting across schools and the hierarchy of sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their roles
Husain Ahmad Madani and Maulana Sayyid Ahmad actively obtained fatawa from Maliki scholars. Recognize that this is a deliberate act of consultation, not random borrowing.
2
Understand the motivation for cross-madhhab consultation
The author mentions the missing person case (mas'alah mafqud) and other incidents. These were cases where Hanafi rulings caused hardship or deadlock, prompting the need for a hila (stratagem) using Maliki opinions.
The missing person case is a well-known difficult area in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Relate to the usul principle of al-istiftah min ghayr al-madhhab
In Hanafi ifta, a mufti may issue a fatwa according to another school when the Hanafi position leads to unavoidable harm (darar) or when necessity (darura) dictates. This is a well-established practice among later Hanafi scholars.
This is not tasahul (laxity) but a recognized method under the maxim 'al-darura tubih al-mahzurat'.
4
Apply the hierarchy of fatwa sources
The primary source is Zahir al-Riwayah (the six books of Imam Muhammad). However, for problematic cases, the mufti may move to the nawadir or even to fatawa of other schools, provided they are correctly transmitted and the need is genuine.
The Maliki fatawa here were likely used as a basis for the hila, not as the primary ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حسین احمد مدنی نے علماء مالکیہ سے قبادی حاصل کرنے میں بہت تعاون فرمایا ، بلکہ مسلہ مفقود کے علاوہ دیگر سواقع میں تحقیق احکام کے اصل محرک بھی وہ ہی میں نیز مدینہ منورہ میں مولانا سید احمد صاحب متهم مدرستہ العلوم الشرعیہ نے علما یہ مالکیہ سے حصول فتادی میں ہر مرتبہ کوشش فرمائی اور ہمیشہ نہایت اہتمام سے فتاوی روانہ فرماتے رہے اور پھر اس رسالہ کا اجمالی مسودہ عزیز نم مولوی ظفر احمد صاحب تھانوی سلمہ نے تیار کیا اور اس کے بعد ان کے رنگون چلے جانے پر اس رسالہ کی تفصیلی ترتیب میں مولوی محمد شفیع صاحب مفتی دارالعلوم دیوبند مولوی عبدالکریم صاحب مشعلی مقیم خانقاہ امدادیہ تھانہ بھون نے بہت مدد دی ہے بلکہ واقع میں قریب قریب رسالہ کی ترتیب ان ہی کا کام ہے اگر چہ بڑا کے نام یہ ناکارہ بھی شریک رہا اس وجہ سے ناظرین پیڑ اپنے ہمراہ ان کے لیے بھی دعا کی گذارش کرتا ہوں ۔ وما توفیقی الا بالله عليه توكلت واليه اشرف علی اوائل ذیقعده ۱۳۵۷ ریه
Husain Ahmad Madani greatly assisted in obtaining fatawa from the Maliki scholars; rather, besides the issue of the missing person, he was also the main motivator for research on rulings in other incidents. Also, in Madinah Munawwarah, Maulana Sayyid Ahmad, in charge of Madrasah al-Uloom al-Shar'iyyah, repeatedly made efforts to obtain fatawa from the Maliki scholars and always sent fatawa with great care. Then, the initial draft of this treatise was prepared by dear Maulana Zafar Ahmad Sahib Thanwi, may he be safe. After he left for Rangoon, in the detailed arrangement of this treatise, Maulana Muhammad Shafi Sahib (Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband) and Maulana Abdul Karim Sahib, a resident of Khanqah Imdadiyyah, Thana Bhawan, gave great help; indeed, the arrangement of the treatise is nearly their work, although the worthless one also participated in the name. Therefore, I request the viewers to include them in your prayers along with me. And my success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely, and to Him I turn. Ashraf Ali, early Dhul Qa'dah 1357 AH.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an acknowledgment by the author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, in which he expresses gratitude to various scholars who assisted in compiling this treatise on legal stratagems (hila). He specifically mentions Husain Ahmad Madani, who helped obtain fatawa from Maliki scholars and was the driving force behind researching several issues beyond the missing person case. Also, Maulana Sayyid Ahmad of Madrasah al-Uloom al-Shar'iyyah in Madinah actively sought Maliki fatawa. The initial draft was prepared by Maulana Zafar Ahmad Thanwi, and after his departure to Rangoon, Maulana Muhammad Shafi (later Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband) and Maulana Abdul Karim (resident of Khanqah Imdadiyyah) completed the detailed arrangement. The author humbly requests readers to include these helpers in their prayers.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hīlah): A legal stratagem or device used to circumvent a difficult ruling in the Hanafi school by adopting a ruling from another school or using a legal nuance.
مسئلہ مفقود (mas'alah al-mafqūd): The legal issue of a missing person whose life status is unknown. Hanafi fiqh has specific rulings on inheritance and marital dissolution after a long wait.
استفتاء من غیر المذهب (al-istiftāh min ghayr al-madhhab): Seeking a fatwa from a school other than one's own (in this case, Hanafi seeking from Maliki).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ashraf Ali Thanwi seek fatawa from Maliki scholars?
A) He was not confident in Hanafi rulings.
B) He needed Maliki fatawa specifically for the missing person case and other incidents where Hanafi rulings caused hardship.
C) He wanted to compile a collection of all schools' rulings.
D) He was asked to do so by the Maliki scholars.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may consult fatawa from other schools in cases of necessity, as demonstrated by the author's practice in compiling his treatise on legal stratagems.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Process of Compiling a Legal Treatise: From Draft to Fatwa
Biographical note on compilation and helpers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the stages of compiling a fatwa collection based on the author's description: initial draft, revision by other scholars, and finalisation.

Core Idea
A reliable fatwa collection is the product of collaborative scholarship, not individual effort.

In his acknowledgments, Ashraf Ali Thanwi describes how the treatise was produced: an initial draft by Maulana Zafar Ahmad Thanwi, followed by detailed arrangement by Maulana Muhammad Shafi and Maulana Abdul Karim after Zafar Ahmad's departure. This reveals the collaborative nature of classical fatwa compilation. In this lesson, we will analyse the steps and the scholarly etiquette involved in publishing a fatwa collection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequential stages of compilation
First, an initial draft (ijmālī musawwadah) was prepared by Zafar Ahmad Thanwi. Then, after his departure, others did a detailed arrangement (tafsīlī tartib).
The author uses the words 'ijmālī' (summary) and 'tafsīlī' (detailed).
2
Note the division of labour
The initial draft captured the core ideas and structure. The later contributors elaborated, organised, and refined the material into its final form.
3
Recognise the author's humility
The author refers to himself as 'this worthless one' and requests prayers for his helpers. This reflects the adab of a scholar: attributing work to others and acknowledging contributions.
4
Connect to the broader practice of fatwa compilation
Many classical fatwa collections were compiled by students or colleagues of the original author, as seen in works like Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya. This lesson highlights how teamwork ensures accuracy and thoroughness.

The initial draft was prepared by Maulana Zafar Ahmad Thanwi, and after his departure to Rangoon, Maulana Muhammad Shafi (later Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband) and Maulana Abdul Karim (resident of Khanqah Imdadiyyah) completed the detailed arrangement. The author humbly requests readers to include these helpers in their prayers.

Key Terms
مسودہ (musawwadah): Draft or initial outline of a written work. In this context, the initial draft of the treatise.
ترتیب (tartīb): Arrangement, organisation, or ordering of content. Here it refers to the detailed arrangement of the treatise's material.
تعاون (ta'āwun): Cooperation, mutual assistance. The passage emphasises the cooperative effort in compiling the treatise.

Husain Ahmad Madani's Role in Motivatoing Research on the Missing Person Case
Biographical note on compilation and helpers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the missing person (mafqud) case in Hanafi fiqh and how it motivated a specific legal stratagem (hila) using Maliki rulings.

Core Idea
The mafqud case, with its long wait in Hanafi law, often requires a hila from another school to avoid hardship.

Ashraf Ali Thanwi specifically mentions that Husain Ahmad Madani was the main motivator for researching the missing person case (mas'alah mafqud) and other incidents. This reveals that the treatise Al-Hilat al-Najijah was born out of a practical need to resolve a difficult case. In this lesson, we will review the Hanafi ruling on mafqud and understand why a hila was needed.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the mention of the missing person case
The passage says: 'besides the issue of the missing person, he was also the main motivator'. This indicates that the treatise was prompted by this specific problem.
2
Recall the Hanafi ruling on mafqud
In Hanafi fiqh, a missing person is presumed alive until either clear evidence of death or until the expiration of his expected lifespan (often set at 90 years). This causes great hardship for the family regarding inheritance and remarriage.
This ruling is based on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity).
3
Understand the need for a hila
To alleviate hardship, the Hanafi school allows using a legal stratagem (hila). In this case, the author sought Maliki fatawa which have a shorter waiting period (e.g., four years of disappearance suffices to declare death).
The Maliki ruling on mafqud is based on qiyas and maslaha.
4
Connect to the purpose of the treatise
The treatise Al-Hilat al-Najijah (The Successful Stratagem) is a collection of such hila for difficult Hanafi cases. The mafqud case is a key example.

The Role of Taqriz and Tasdiqat in the Hanafi Fatwa Tradition
Endorsements and taqriz for the treatise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of taqriz in the Hanafi madrasa tradition and explain how endorsements from recognized institutions contribute to the authority of a fiqh work.

Core Idea
Taqriz authenticates a text; it is paratextual but signals authority within the Hanafi tradition.

The front matter of a Hanafi fiqh work often includes tasdiqat—endorsements from senior scholars and institutions. This lesson examines the taqriz from Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi for al-Hilatul Najijah. Though not legally binding, such endorsements establish a work's reliability and facilitate its acceptance as a mufta bihi reference. Understanding this paratextual apparatus is key to navigating classical fiqh and fatwa resources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of text
Recognize that the passage is front matter (tasdiqat and taqriz), not a legal ruling or proof. This paratext serves to introduce and authenticate the work.
2
List the endorsing entities
Note the seminaries: Imdad al-Ulum Thana Bhawan, Dar al-Ulum Deoband, and Mazahir al-Ulum Saharanpur. Their collective endorsement adds weight.
These are major Hanafi institutions in South Asia.
3
Analyze the language of praise
Examine the exaggerated praise: 'unique pearl', 'life for dead truth', 'death for false statement'. This indicates the work is seen as solving a critical problem.
Such language is conventional but signals high esteem.
4
Correlate with legal content
Understand that the treatise addresses a pressing issue for the ummah (likely regarding prayer). The endorsement assures readers that the work is beneficial and reliable.
The exact issue is not detailed here, but the context suggests it is a fiqh/iftaa matter.
5
Explain the fatwa hierarchy implication
Endorsements like these contribute to a work's mufta bihi status. They do not replace textual evidence but certify that the work has been vetted by established scholars.
A mufti may rely on such endorsed works with greater confidence.

These endorsements serve to authenticate and recommend the work to the scholarly community.

تقریظ (taqriz): A laudatory preface or testimonial written by a scholar for a book, praising its content and author.

Endorsements and Conditions: The Authority of Al-Hilat al-Najizah
Endorsements and requests to adhere to conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions required for applying the ḥīlah in this treatise and explain the authority of the endorsements in the Hanafi iftā’ tradition.

Core Idea
A ḥīlah is valid only if all its conditions are strictly observed; endorsements confirm authority, not leniency.

The front matter of a scholarly work often carries endorsements (taṣdīqāt) from senior authorities, which serve to validate its content and remind readers of its proper use. In this passage, prominent Hanafi scholars of India praise ‘Al-Hilat al-Najizah’ for solving a critical community problem, but they equally stress that its conditions are non-negotiable. This lesson will help you understand the role of endorsements in establishing a work’s authority and the ethical obligation to adhere to stipulated conditions when issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the function of endorsements
Identify that the endorsements (taṣdīqāt) by scholars like Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi and Dar al-Ulum Deoband serve to certify the treatise’s reliability and its compliance with the Hanafi school, ensuring it is not a deviant innovation.
Endorsements do not make a weak opinion strong; they confirm that the work meets scholarly standards.
2
Extract the key conditions emphasized
From the text, note the repeated insistence on ‘quyūd wa sharā’iṭ’ (conditions and stipulations). The scholars explicitly state that these conditions are extremely necessary and must be kept in sight during practice.
The ḥīlah is not a free pass; it is a precisely defined legal device.
3
Understand the warning against misuse
The text warns against using ‘mere necessity’ as an excuse to abandon the conditions, which would lead to following desires (ittibā‘ hawā). This is a critical ethical boundary for both the layperson and the mufti.
Necessity (ḍarūrah) must be genuine and strictly limited.
4
Determine the mufti’s responsibility
The request to muftis is to ‘take all conditions well in view and specify them’ when issuing a fatwa. This means the mufti must not only know the conditions but also articulate them in the fatwa to prevent misunderstanding.
A fatwa without conditions can lead to widespread misapplication.
5
Apply the lesson to the overall case
Understand that the treatise addresses the problem of a missing husband (mafqūd). The endorsements and conditions are not abstract; they apply directly to this real-life scenario, providing a structured solution when all conditions are met.
The ḥīlah is for those who truly have no alternative.

This unique treatise has filled my eyes with the light of those precious pearls. I found it unique in its chapter, a priceless pearl brought out from the depths of the sea. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Endorsements of the great scholars of India. After praise and salutations, it is submitted that this treatise, full of grace, is evidently extremely necessary, and its comprehensive, restrictive, and highly beneficial nature is needless of explanation. Even a cursory glance at it spontaneously says: 'From far to near, everywhere I look, a gesture grabs the skirt of the heart, saying: The place is here.' In reality, the solution to this important difficulty of the deceased community needed someone like His Holiness, who is a collection of perfections. He exerted extreme thought and scrutiny over a long period in this research and composition. Only those who had the fortune of being present during the time of its composition can estimate its value. His Holiness repeatedly stated: 'I have not faced such difficulty in any work in my entire life.' May Allah Most High keep the shadow of mercy of His Holiness (may his blessings endure) permanent over our heads. Amen, then Amen. Now, the only request to those in need is that the conditions and stipulations mentioned in this treatise are extremely necessary. At the time of practice, keep them well in sight and fully adhere to them. Do not fall into following desires using the excuse of necessity. Also, from those who issue fatwas, with utmost humility, it is requested that when giving fatwa, they must keep all conditions well in view and consider it necessary to specify them. And He is the One who grants success to good and prevents from every evil. The petitioner - the least of servants, the lowest of slaves, the humble 'Abd al-Karim, may he be pardoned, from Khanqah Imdadpur, 1352 AH, Thana Bhawan, dated 27 Ramadan 5? al-Rahman. Wait. Siraj Ahmad, may he be forgiven, teacher at Khanqah Imdadi. In every Ramadan al-Mubarak, 1357 AH. Band? Shahrdaran? Jamid? Deoband we? From Dar al-'Ulum Deoband: All of us have carefully studied the treatise 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah lil-Hilat al-'Ajizah'. Indeed, in our Indian region, under current circumstances, no alternative seems possible except that the scholars of the Hanafi school adopt the issues mentioned in this treatise as operative and give fatwa accordingly. In past centuries, the Hanafi scholars also [did so] in the case of a missing person, etc.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is from the front matter of 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah', containing endorsements (taṣdīqāt) by prominent Hanafi scholars of India, including Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi and 'Abd al-Karim from Khanqah Imdadpur, as well as an endorsement by scholars of Dar al-'Ulum Deoband. The comments praise the treatise for its unprecedented benefit in solving critical problems faced by the Muslim community, especially in matters where legal stratagems (ḥiyal) are needed. They emphasize that the conditions and stipulations (quyūd wa sharā'iṭ) recorded in the treatise are extremely important and must be strictly observed. The scholars warn against using the excuse of necessity to abandon these conditions, which would lead to following desires. They also request muftis to ensure all conditions are considered when issuing fatwas based on this work. This front matter establishes the authoritative and practical importance of the treatise for the Hanafi school in the Indian subcontinent.

Key Terms
حيلة (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem or device used to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding a prohibition or fulfilling a requirement when the direct path is blocked.
قود و شرائط (quyūd wa sharā’iṭ): Conditions and stipulations that must be fulfilled for the ḥīlah to be valid.
تصدیقات (taṣdīqāt): Endorsements or approvals by qualified scholars, certifying the reliability and correctness of a work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Endorsements confirm a work’s authority but do not relax its conditions; strict adherence to all stipulated conditions is mandatory for valid application.

Scholarly Endorsements and the Principle of Adopting Other Madhhabs
Endorsements by scholars affirming the author's authority and the principle of adopting other madhhabs in necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that allows a mufti to adopt another madhhab in severe necessity and identify the basis for this in the scholarly endorsements.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti may adopt another madhhab when severe necessity demands it—this is itself a ruling of Hanafi fiqh.

This concluding section of 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah' contains scholarly endorsements that not only praise the author but also affirm a critical principle of Hanafi ifta': the permissibility of following another madhhab under necessity. Understanding this principle is essential for muftis facing modern challenges where strict adherence to the dominant view may cause hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the passage
Recognize that this is an endorsement (taqriz) by scholars, not a legal ruling itself. It confirms the author's credibility and the work's reliability.
2
Extract the key legal principle
The scholars state that in times of severe necessity (darurah), a Hanafi mufti may adopt the madhhab of another imam for issuing fatwas. This permissibility is itself a ruling of the Hanafi school.
The passage explicitly says: '…because in times of severe necessity, adopting the madhhab of other imams is also a ruling of Hanafi fiqh.'
3
Note the practical implication
This principle allows flexibility in ifta' when strict adherence to the Hanafi position causes undue hardship. It empowers the mufti to choose a valid opinion from another school to alleviate difficulty.

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of the book 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah', containing endorsements (taqrizat) from prominent scholars of the Indian subcontinent. The text explains that the author, Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, being a master jurist, has the right to adopt rulings from other madhhabs when necessary—a principle recognized in Hanafi fiqh. The endorsing scholars affirm the work's quality and its adherence to the rules of ifta'. This section is not a legal ruling but a scholarly validation of the author's methodology and the compilation's reliability.

Key Terms
تقريظ (taqriz): An endorsement or commendation of a scholarly work by other established scholars.
فتوى (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified mufti.
ضرورت شدیدہ (darurah shadidah): Severe necessity that justifies exceptional rulings, such as adopting another madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Endorsements and the Principle of Adopting Other Madhhabs
Concluding endorsements and title page of a treatise on dissolution of marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of scholarly endorsements (taqriz) in establishing the authority of a Hanafi fatwa work and explain the Hanafi principle that permits adopting another madhhab in times of necessity.

Core Idea
Endorsements confirm the author's authority; the Hanafi school permits adopting other madhhabs when necessity demands.

This passage presents the endorsements of notable scholars—including Muhammad Zakariyya Kandhlawi—for Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi's treatise on dissolution of marriage, al-Mukhtarat fi Muhimmat al-Tafriq wa al-Khiyarat. The endorsements highlight a key Hanafi legal principle: in times of extreme necessity, a mufti may adopt the ruling of another madhhab. This lesson unpacks the significance of these endorsements and the underlying rule that allows flexibility in fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage structure
Recognize that this is front matter: endorsements (taqriz) followed by the title page. The endorsements are from multiple scholars, each affirming the author's competence and the work's reliability.
Endorsements are not legal rulings but attestations of authority.
2
Understand the purpose of endorsements
Scholarly endorsements serve to certify the author's qualifications and the work's adherence to sound methodology, increasing trust among those who seek fatwa from the work.
In Hanafi tradition, taqriz by established scholars lends weight to a text.
3
Recognize the Hanafi principle of adopting other madhhabs
The endorsements explicitly state that in times of extreme necessity (shidda), a Hanafi mufti may adopt the position of another imam, as this is itself a ruling within the Hanafi school ( based on the principle that necessity permits otherwise restricted actions).
This is a key principle in Usul al-Iftaa: talfiq and takhayyur under necessity.
4
Note the title and publication details
The title 'al-Mukhtarat fi Muhimmat al-Tafriq wa al-Khiyarat' and the fourth edition date (Shawwal 1373 AH) indicate the work's subject matter and its continued relevance.
The title reflects the content: selections on dissolution of marriage and options.
5
Appreciate the significance for fatwa authority
This front matter establishes that the treatise is a reliable reference for muftis facing difficult marriage dissolution cases, especially when Hanafi rulings need supplementation from other madhhabs.
Understanding endorsements helps evaluate the weight of a fatwa source.

They affirm that his work on dissolution of marriage (faskh al-nikah) is thorough and reliable. The second part gives the title of the treatise: 'al-Mukhtarat fi Muhimmat al-Tafriq wa al-Khiyarat' (Selections on Important Matters of Dissolution and Options), with publication details (fourth edition, Shawwal 1373 AH). This demonstrates the scholarly reception and authority of the work.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Methodology for Adding Three Cases of Faskh Nikah
Describing the need and methodology for adding three new cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodology used by Ashraf Ali Thanwi in supplementing the original treatise with three additional cases of faskh nikah, including the role of the Maliki madhhab and the use of Hanafi texts and qawaid.

Core Idea
The supplement extends the original necessity-based fatwa by using Maliki rulings for the committee and Hanafi texts for other parts.

After completing the original treatise 'Al-Hilat an-Najizah' on faskh nikah in the absence of a qadi, Ashraf Ali Thanwi identified three more cases requiring dissolution. This supplement explains how these cases were addressed, building on the earlier methodology of a Muslim community committee acting as a substitute qadi following the Maliki madhhab, while using Hanafi fiqh texts for non-committee aspects and consulting scholars where needed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The original treatise solved the problem of faskh nikah when no Sharia qadi is available. The supplement adds three more cases: Dast-e-Musaharat, Khiyar-e-Ghurkh, and Khiyar-e-Kafa'at.
These cases were not part of the original five.
2
Identify the committee's madhhab
The Muslim community committee, acting as a substitute qadi, follows the Maliki madhhab for its decisions, as established in the original treatise.
This is a necessity-based departure from the Hanafi madhhab.
3
Recognize the supplement's sources
For non-committee matters, the supplement primarily uses Hanafi fiqh texts. Only a few rulings were derived from qawaid after consulting scholars of Deoband.
The author notes where direct texts are lacking.
4
Note the treatment of uncertainty
When there was consensus, the ruling was given definitively with a reference to the principle; otherwise, hesitation or difference was noted.
This reflects careful iftaa methodology.
5
Apply the methodology
The same approach can be used today: form a committee following Maliki rules for faskh nikah when no qadi is available, and use Hanafi texts for other related issues.
This is a practical fatwa hierarchy.
