اب ان کی بقدر ضرورت تفصیل لکھی جاتی ہے۔ پور سے احکام بوقت ضرورت علماء کرام کتب فقہ میں ملاحظہ فرمائیں۔ اور عوام ملمائے کرام سے دریافت کرنیں۔
Supplement to the treatise titled 'Al-Mukhtarat' concerning important matters of separation and options. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After praise and salutations, it is stated that for those issues where the need for dissolution of marriage or separation by a qadi arises, and due to the absence of a qadi, there is difficulty in the time, the treatise 'Al-Hilat an-Najizah li al-Aylah al-Ajizah' was written with great verification and precision after consultation with many verifying scholars. And in it, it was unanimously decided that in India, wherever a Sharia qadi is not present, and it is not possible to obtain a Sharia verdict from a Muslim ruler's court, then a committee of Muslims (i.e., a Sharia committee) shall be considered as the acting qadi in accordance with the Maliki madhhab. After the completion of this treatise, it was felt necessary that besides the five issues mentioned in the treatise, there are three more situations where the need for dissolution of marriage arises and difficulties occur due to the absence of a qadi. These were also to be included in this treatise so that all necessary issues are collected together. But these three issues were not presented before all the mentioned scholars, the reason being that presenting before all would cause great delay, and moreover, great necessity was not felt in these issues, because most of them were a decision of the consultative part of the committee [?] which was taken from the Maliki madhhab, and that has already been settled in the original treatise with the consultation of scholars. Therefore, assuming distinction [?], these three issues are being attached as a supplement with a separate name. Apart from the committee of Muslims, the remaining parts of this supplement are taken from the fiqh books of our own madhhab, in which most, rather almost all, issues are explicitly stated as will be known from the included quotations. Only in two or four places, due to the lack of explicit text, derivation from principles was necessary. In those, reference was made to the scholars of Deoband Saharanpur. Where something was unanimously settled, the ruling was written with certainty and the fiqh principle was indicated; otherwise, hesitation or difference was written. And those three issues are: Dast-e-Musaharat, Khiyar-e-Ghurkh, Khiyar-e-Kafa'at. Now their detail is being written to the extent of necessity. The complete rulings, when needed, scholars may observe in the fiqh books, and the common people should ask the scholars.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a front matter introduction to a supplement (tammah) of the original risala 'Al-Hilat an-Najizah' by Ashraf Ali Thanwi. It explains the methodology used: The original treatise dealt with five cases requiring faskh nikah in the absence of a qadi, and it established that a Muslim community committee acts as a substitute qadi following the Maliki madhhab. After its completion, three more cases were identified: Dast-e-Musaharat (marriage by handshake?), Khiyar-e-Ghurkh (option of fraud), and Khiyar-e-Kafa'at (option of equality). These were not presented to the full panel of scholars to avoid delay, and they rely mostly on the Maliki madhhab as already decided. The supplement is appended as a separate named part. For the non-Maliki parts, the author primarily used Hanafi fiqh texts, and only in a few instances derived rulings from legal maxims after consulting the scholars of Deoband. Where there was consensus, the ruling was given definitively with a reference to the principle; otherwise, uncertainty or disagreement was noted. This reflects the Hanafi fatwa methodology of resorting to other madhahib under necessity and relying on qawaid when direct texts are unavailable.

Key Terms
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikah): Judicial dissolution of marriage, distinct from talaq (divorce by husband's initiative).
قاضی شرعی (qadi shar'i): A judge appointed by a Muslim ruler or elected by the community to adjudicate according to Sharia.
مذہب مالکی (madhhab Maliki): The Maliki school of Islamic law, used here as the basis for the committee's decisions in the absence of a Hanafi qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when the supplement's rulings are not explicitly found in the fiqh books, what does the author do?
A) Consults scholars of Deoband
B) Relies on qiyas alone
C) Leaves the issue undecided
D) Refers to the Maliki madhhab

Key Takeaway
The supplement demonstrates a nuanced iftaa methodology that blends Maliki rulings for the committee, Hanafi texts, and consultation with scholars to address new fiqh needs.

Methodology of Al-Hilatul Najijah: Source and Deduction
Author explains source material and compilation method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's method for deriving rulings, distinguishing between explicit textual rulings and those deduced from qawāʿid.

Core Idea
Most rulings are directly from Hanafi texts; only a few require deduction from principles.

In this introductory passage, Ashraf Ali Thanwi explains how he compiled Al-Hilatul Najijah. He relied primarily on explicit Hanafi fiqh books, and only in rare cases did he need to deduce rulings from legal maxims (qawāʿid). When deduction was needed, he consulted scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur. This lesson will help you understand the methodology behind the treatise and the value of both textual transmission and principled reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary source
Recognize that the author's main reliance is on explicit texts from Hanafi fiqh books. Nearly all rulings are taken directly from these sources.
The author states 'اکثر بلکہ تقریباً کل مسائل مصرح ہیں' (most, indeed nearly all, issues are explicit).
2
Locate the exceptions
Find where deduction from principles was necessary: only in two or four places ( دو چار جگہ ) where explicit text was lacking.
This shows the limited scope of qawāʿid-based derivation in this treatise.
3
Note the consultation process
Understand that when deduction was required, the author consulted scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur. If agreement was reached, the ruling was stated with certainty and a pointer to the fiqh maxim; otherwise, hesitation or disagreement was recorded.
This emphasizes scholarly consultation as a safeguard against error.
4
Identify the three specific issues
Record the three issues that needed special treatment: دست مصاہرت (handshake leading to marriage prohibition), خیار گورخ (option of inspection), and خیار کفایت (option of equality in marriage). These are detailed later in the treatise.
These are the cases where explicit text was not readily available.
5
Differentiate the audience
Notice the author's direction: scholars may look into full fiqh books for complete rulings, while laypeople should ask the learned scholars.
This reflects the hanafi principle of taqlid and the importance of scholarly authority.

بمشورہ علماء کرام طے ہو چکا ہے۔ اس لیے بفرض امتیازان مسائل ثلتہ کو مستقل نام سے موسوم کر کے بطور تمہ ملحق کیا جاتا ہے اور جماعت مسلمین کے علاوہ اس تمہ کے باقی اجزاء اپنے مذہب کی کتب فقہ سے لیے گئے ہیں جن میں اکثر بلکہ تقریباً کل مسائل مصرح ہیں جیسا کہ عبارات مندرجہ سے معلوم ہوگا صرف دو چار جگہ تصریح نہ ملنے کی باعث قواعد سے استنباط کی نوبت آئی ہے اُن میں علمائے دیوبند سہارنپور سے مراجعت کی گئی ۔ جہاں بالاتفاق کچھ طے ہو گیا وہاں جزم کے ساتھ مسئلہ لکھ کر قاعدہ فقیہہ کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا ورنہ تردد یا اختلاف لکھ دیا اور وہ تین مسائل یہ ہیں ۔ دست مصاہرت خیار گورخ - خیار کفاوت اب ان کی بقدر ضرورت تفصیل لکھی جاتی ہے۔ پور سے احکام بوقت ضرورت علماء کرام کتب فقہ میں ملاحظہ فرمائیں۔ اور عوام ملمائے کرام سے دریافت کرنیں۔
It has been settled by consultation with the noble scholars. Therefore, assuming distinction, the three issues are named independently and attached as an introduction. Apart from the Muslim community, the remaining parts of this introduction are taken from the fiqh books of our madhhab, in which most, indeed nearly all, issues are explicit, as will be known from the included texts. Only in two or four places, due to lack of explicit text, the need for deduction from principles arose. In those, reference was made to the scholars of Deoband and Saharanpur. Where something was unanimously settled, the ruling was written with certainty and a pointer to the fiqh maxim was given; otherwise, hesitation or disagreement was written. Those three issues are: Dast Musaharat, Khiyar Gorkh, Khiyar Kafa'at. Now their detail is written to the extent necessary. For complete rulings, when needed, the noble scholars may look into fiqh books, and the common people should inquire from the learned scholars.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction by the author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explaining the compilation process of his treatise 'Al-Hilatul Najijah'. He states that the majority of rulings are taken directly from Hanafi fiqh texts, with only a few instances requiring deduction from legal principles (qawa'id). In those cases, he consulted scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur, recording either a definitive ruling with a reference to the maxim, or noting hesitation or disagreement. Three specific issues are singled out for treatment: Dast Musaharat (handshake leading to marriage prohibition), Khiyar Gorkh (option of inspection), and Khiyar Kafa'at (option of equality in marriage). The author directs scholars to refer to full fiqh books for complete details and advises laypeople to ask the learned.

Key Terms
قواعد (qawāʿid): Legal maxims or principles from which rulings are deduced when explicit texts are not available.
استنباط (istinbāṭ): Deduction of a legal ruling from foundational principles.
دست مصاہرت (dast muṣāharat): Handshake that leads to prohibition of marriage (due to the implication of intimacy).
خیار گورخ (khiyār gūrkh): Option of inspection; the buyer's right to cancel a sale after inspecting the goods.
خیار کفایت (khiyār kafā'ah): Option of equality in marriage; the right of a woman or her guardian to annul a marriage if the husband is not socially equal (kufʾ).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many issues required deduction from principles according to the passage?
A) Two
B) Four
C) Three
D) Five

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti's primary source is explicit texts; deduction from qawāʿid and consultation are secondary and used only when texts are silent.

Understanding the Colophon and Endorsements of al-Hilat al-Najijah
Colophon with completion details and scholarly endorsements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's teacher and explain the significance of scholarly endorsements (taqriz) in authenticating a Hanafi fatwa work.

Core Idea
Colophons and endorsements certify a work's transmission and scholarly authority.

The concluding pages of al-Hilat al-Najijah contain more than just a date. They reveal the author's teacher, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, and include endorsements from prominent Hanafi scholars like Mufti Muhammad Shafi'. This lesson decodes that colophon and explains why such endorsements matter for fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and teacher
From the colophon, locate the author's name (Abdul Karim) and his teacher (Ashraf Ali Thanwi). Understand the reverence expressed through titles.
Author humility: describes himself as 'the most contemptible of creatures'.
2
Locate completion details
Find the date and place: completion in early Ramadan 1352 AH. Note the use of 'Ramadan' and the hijri year.
This places the work in the early 20th century CE.
3
Recognize the function of taqriz
Identify the endorsements from Muhammad Shafi', Siraj Ahmad, and Zafar Ahmad. Understand that taqriz serves to verify the work's correctness and scholarly acceptance.
Endorsements are not part of the original text; they are added later by reviewers.
4
Evaluate the scholarly chain
Trace the chain from author to teacher to endorsers. Recognize how this chain strengthens the authority of the work for fatwa.
Muhammad Shafi' was the Grand Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband.

The judgment of a judge came with the condition of all except ownership, love, and Islam which includes kissing of a captive with ila' or original separation when the contract ends with her hands, and here the supplement is proven. The supplement containing important issues related to calamitous incidents by the success of the One in Whose hand is the knot of matters and crises – in the beginning of a blessed month from the Sovereign, the Judge, and He cancels for whom He wills the gate of al-Rayyan, known as the month of Ramadan, whose beginning is mercy, middle is forgiveness, and end is freedom from fire, in the year 1352 after the Prophet's emigration – upon him a thousand thousand salutations and greetings – by the hand of the most contemptible of creatures and the most humble, His sinful slave hoping for His abundant grace, called Abdul Karim, may Allah cover his sin, the small and the great of it, and save him from his evil and old habits. Indeed He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful. And this weak slave in composing this treatise and writing this quick work is like the movement of a shadow after an eye and a pen between two fingers. It is its beginning and end, its entirety and detail, from the outpourings of the confluence of two seas and the source of two rivers, the green of the path, the sweet of the Sharia, the remainder of the predecessors, the proof of the successors, the sage of the nation in every distress – our master, the pious, the saintly, the sublime, famously known as Ashraf Ali, may he remain immersed in the oceans of His subtle grace and manifestation. May Allah grant us benefit from his long life and perennial blessings. Praise be to Allah, by Whose might and majesty good works are completed. Peace and blessings be upon the Master of existences.

Endorsements
We looked at the supplement and found it correct. I was honored to study this supplement and found it more excellent than a precious stone on the eleventh of Ramadan... so may Allah reward the one who made it a pearl.
The weak slave Muhammad Shafi' his virtue servant, extracted it and adorned it for two months and sold it; may Allah reward him.
Allah forgive.
Dar al-Ifta Deoband
Siraj Ahmad, forgive him, teacher at Khanqah Imdadiyyah.
May Allah reward me and all Muslims with the best and most excellent reward, and grant me and him a good life and a good end. I am the sinful slave.
Zafar Ahmad, may Allah forgive him, 29 Ramadan 35 ...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is the colophon and endorsement section (التتمة والتقريظ) of al-Hilat al-Najijah. The author, Abdul Karim (likely a student of Ashraf Ali Thanwi), states that he completed this supplement (تتمة) in early Ramadan 1352 AH. He praises his teacher Ashraf Ali Thanwi as 'the green of the path, the sweet of the Sharia, the remainder of the predecessors, the proof of the successors, the sage of the nation.' The passage then includes endorsements from scholars such as Muhammad Shafi' (Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband), Siraj Ahmad, and Zafar Ahmad, attesting to the correctness of the work. The fragmented sentences between colophon and endorsements seem to be stray legal notes about ila' (vow of abstinence) and zihar (like mother), but are too corrupt to extract a coherent ruling. This section is valuable for understanding the scholarly chain and reception of the work.

Key Terms
تتمة (tatimmah): A supplement or completion to a main work; in this context, it refers to the additional material appended to al-Hilat al-Najijah.
تقريظ (taqrīẓ): Endorsement or commendation written by scholars to approve a work.
شهر رمضان (shahr Ramaḍān): The month of Ramadan, mentioned as the time of completion of the supplement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The colophon and endorsements authenticate al-Hilat al-Najijah and connect it to the scholarly lineage of Ashraf Ali Thanwi and Mufti Muhammad Shafi'.

Understanding a Hanafi Colophon: Ijazah and Authority
Colophon with scholarly approvals and title of appended treatise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of a classical Hanafi colophon (ijazah, tatimma, dar al-ifta) and explain their function in establishing the chain of transmission and fatwa authority.

Core Idea
A colophon is not just a closing; it is a legal certification of a text's reliability and authorized transmission.

This lesson examines a colophon from Al-Hilatul Najijah, a work on legal stratagems (hiyal) in Hanafi fiqh. The colophon contains endorsements from scholars of Dar al-Ifta Deoband, which serve as a formal ijazah (license) affirming the correctness of the supplement (tatimma). Understanding such paratextual elements is essential for evaluating the authority of a text in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main components
Scan the Arabic text for key terms like 'التتمة' (supplement), 'دار الافتاء' (fatwa institution), and scholar names. These tell you about the text's provenance and verification.
Notice the phrase 'نظرنا في التتمة فوجدناها صحيحة' – a standard formula of endorsement.
2
Analyze the chain of certifiers
Extract the names mentioned: Muhammad Shafi', Siraj Ahmad, Zafar Ahmad. Understand their roles – revisers, teachers, or muftis. This chain links the text to the Deoband scholarly network.
These scholars are part of the Hanafi tradition rooted in the Indian subcontinent.
3
Decipher dates and places
Look for dates (e.g., '11th of Ramadan', '29 Ramadan 35?') and place names ('Deoband', 'Thanah Bhavan'). These contextualize when and where the certifications were made.
The incomplete year '35' likely refers to a Hijri century, e.g., 13?? AH.
4
Identify the appended treatise
The second part on page 174 gives a title: 'Shariah rulings of marriage with non-Muslims'. This suggests the volume contains multiple works, a common practice in classical publishing.
The phrase 'يعني' indicates an explanation of the title.
5
Evaluate the authority level
Consider that a colophon with endorsements from recognized dar al-ifta and scholars makes the text part of the mufta bihi tradition. Its rulings carry weight in legal practice.
Compare with works that lack such endorsements – they may be less authoritative.

Commentary
This passage is a colophon containing certifications and approvals for the book 'Al-Hilatul Najijah'. The scholars of Dar al-Ifta Deoband and Khanqah Imdadiyyah verify the supplement (tatimma) of the book. The text includes the names of Muhammad Shafi', Siraj Ahmad, and Zafar Ahmad, who are likely the revisers or certifiers. The second part on page 174 appears to be the title of an appended treatise on the shariah rulings of marriage with non-Muslims, suggesting this volume may include multiple works.

Key Terms
التتمة (al-tatimma): The supplement or appendix to the main book, here specifically certified by scholars.
دار الافتاء (dar al-ifta): The institution for issuing fatwas, here specifically Deoband.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): A license or certification, here indicating the text has been approved for use.
التصديقات (al-tasdiqat): Certifications or endorsements, synonymous with ijazat.

Background and Purpose of the Supplement on Marital Religious Difference
Editor's preface introducing supplementary treatise on marital issues due to religious difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and scope of the supplement Hukm al-Izdawaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Din al-Azwaj and state the two key questions it addresses.

Core Idea
This supplement clarifies marital rulings when spouses differ in religion, specifically apostasy of the wife.

This passage is the editor's preface explaining why this supplement was added to Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najizah. It highlights two crucial questions: does a woman's apostasy annul the marriage, and can she remarry after reverting to Islam?

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and context
Read the opening lines to understand who is writing and why. Editor Muhammad Shafi Deobandi is acting on a directive from Hadrat Thanwi to append these rulings.
Thanwi is the original author of Al-Hilat al-Najizah; Shafi compiles the supplement.
2
List the two key questions
The supplement aims to clarify two specific issues: (1) whether a woman's apostasy annuls the marriage, and (2) whether after reverting to Islam she can marry another person.
Both questions revolve around the effect of apostasy on the continuity of the nikah.
3
Note the supplement's name and relation
The supplement is titled Hukm al-Izdawaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Din al-Azwaj. It is an appendix to the original work, not a standalone treatise.

حضرت امام العارفين سراج الساكين خضر الطريقي منظر التوفيق فقيه حکیم الامت مجدد الملت سیدی وسندی حضرت مولانا اشرف علی صاحب تھانوی دامت برکا تہم نے اپنے رسالہ الحیلۃ الناجزه للحملة العاجزہ کی تمہید میں حاشیہ پر تحریر فرمایا ہے کہ چند مسائل متعلقہ ازدواج بصورت اختلاف مذہب کا اضافہ بطور ضمیمہ کیا جائے گا جس میں خصوصیت سے یہ بات بھی واضح کی جائے گی کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے سے نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے یا نہیں اور بعد تجدید اسلام دوسرے شخص سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے یا نہیں ؟ حضرت اقدس نے قلت فرصت کی وجہ سے اس ناکارہ غلام کو ارشاد فرمایا اس لیے تعمیل ارشاد کے لیے یہ رسالہ لکھ کر حضرت کی خدمت میں پیش کیا اور نام اس کا حکم الازدواج مع اختلاف دین الازواج تجویز ہوا حق تعالیٰ اس کو بھی اصل رسالہ کی طرح مفید اور مقبول فرمائے اور حضرت کے فیوض سے متمتع فرمائے ۔ آمین بنده محمد شفیع دیوبندی غفرله شادم دار الافتاء دیوبند
Hadrat Imam al-Arifin, Siraj al-Salikin, Khidr al-Tariqi, Manzar al-Tawfiq, Faqih Hakim al-Ummah, Mujaddid al-Millat, my master and support, Hadrat Maulana Ashraf Ali Sahib Thanwi (may his blessings endure) wrote in the margins of the preface of his treatise Al-Hilat al-Najizah li al-Hamlat al-Ajizah that several marital issues concerning difference of religion will be added as an appendix, in which it will be particularly clarified whether marriage is annulled by a woman's apostasy or not, and whether after renewing Islam, marriage with another person is permissible or not. His Holiness, due to lack of time, directed this incapable slave, so to comply, this treatise was written and presented to His Holiness, and its name was suggested as Hukm al-Izdawaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Din al-Azwaj. May Allah make it beneficial and accepted like the original treatise, and grant benefit from His Holiness's blessings. Amen. The servant Muhammad Shafi Deobandi (may Allah forgive him), Shadim Dar al-Ifta, Deoband.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a preface by the editor, Muhammad Shafi Deobandi, explaining the background of the supplementary treatise. He states that Hadrat Thanwi directed him to add a supplement covering marital issues arising from religious differences, specifically whether a woman's apostasy annuls the marriage and whether she can remarry after reverting to Islam. The editor compiled this supplement and named it Hukm al-Izdawaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Din al-Azwaj. He prays for its acceptance.

نکاح (nikah): Marriage contract
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage contract
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate, one who leaves Islam

Preface to Hukm al-Azwaj Supplement: Authorship and Purpose
Front matter describing the composition of a fiqh supplement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the occasion, author, and scope of the supplement Hukm al-Azwaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Deen al-Azwaj.

Core Idea
Ashraf Ali Thanwi delegated the composition of a crucial supplement on apostasy and marriage to his disciple Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi.

This passage introduces the supplementary treatise Hukm al-Azwaj, written by Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi under the guidance of Ashraf Ali Thanwi. It clarifies the key issues addressed: the effect of a wife's apostasy on marriage and remarriage after return to Islam. Understanding the provenance and scope of this work is essential for modern fatwa practice on similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and delegator
Determine who wrote the supplement (Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi) and who delegated it (Ashraf Ali Thanwi). Note the respectful titles used.
The phrase 'ghulam' (slave) indicates the disciple's humility.
2
Note the original work
Identify the main treatise that prompted the supplement: Al-Hilatun Najizah li al-Hamlat al-Ajizah. Understand that the supplement is an appendix to this work.
Al-Hilatun Najizah is a collection of legal stratagems.
3
List the specific legal questions
Extract the two questions mentioned: (1) whether marriage is annulled by a woman's apostasy, and (2) whether she can remarry after returning to Islam.
These become the focus of the supplement.
4
Recognize the title and purpose
The supplement is titled Hukm al-Azwaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Deen al-Azwaj. Its purpose is to address marriage rulings when spouses differ in religion, particularly apostasy.
The title literally means 'The Ruling of Spouses with Difference of Religion of the Spouses'.

Hadrat Imam al-Arifin, Siraj al-Salikin, Khidr al-Tariqi, Manzar al-Tawfiq, Faqih, Hakim al-Ummah, Mujaddid al-Millat, Sayyidi wa Sanadi, Hadrat Mawlana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, may his blessings continue, wrote in a marginal note in the preface of his treatise Al-Hilatun Najizah li al-Hamlat al-Ajizah that a few issues regarding marriage in case of difference of religion will be added as an appendix, in which it will be particularly clarified whether marriage is annulled by a woman's apostasy or not, and whether after renewal of Islam, marriage to another person is permissible or not. Due to lack of opportunity, Hadrat Aqdas instructed this incapable slave, so for compliance with the instruction, I wrote this treatise and presented it to Hadrat, and its name was decided as Hukm al-Azwaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Deen al-Azwaj. May Allah make it beneficial and accepted like the original treatise, and may He grant enjoyment of Hadrat's blessings. Ameen. The slave Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi, may Allah forgive him. Dar al-Ifta, Deoband.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a front matter/preface to a supplementary treatise on marital rulings when spouses differ in religion. It explains the genesis of the supplement: the eminent Hanafi scholar Mawlana Ashraf Ali Thanwi (d. 1943) had indicated in his main work 'Al-Hilatun Najizah' that such a supplement was needed, particularly to address the question of whether a wife's apostasy annuls the marriage and whether she can remarry after returning to Islam. Due to his own lack of time, he delegated the task to his disciple Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi (later Mufti of Pakistan). This preface, written by Shafi', confirms the completion of the work titled 'Hukm al-Azwaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Deen al-Azwaj' (The Ruling of Spouses with Difference of Religion of the Spouses) and expresses hope for its acceptance. The passage sets the context for the legal discussions that follow in the supplement.

Key Terms
رسالہ الحیلۃ الناجزه للحملة العاجزہ (Risalah al-Hilatun Najizah li al-Hamlat al-Ajizah): The main treatise by Ashraf Ali Thanwi on legal stratagems (hiyal) for difficult situations.
حكم الازدواج مع اختلاف دين الازواج (Hukm al-Azwaj ma'a Ikhtilaf Deen al-Azwaj): The title of the supplementary treatise meaning 'The Ruling of Spouses with Difference of Religion of the Spouses'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The supplement Hukm al-Azwaj was written by Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi under Thanwi's instruction to address marriage rulings in cases of religious difference, especially apostasy.

Understanding Taṣdīqāt: Scholarly Endorsements in the Hanafi Tradition
Collection of endorsements from senior Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of taṣdīqāt in a Hanafi fiqh work and identify their role in establishing scholarly authority.

Core Idea
Taṣdīqāt certify a book's correctness through senior scholars' approval, a cornerstone of Hanafi authority.

This passage presents a collection of endorsements (taṣdīqāt) from prominent Hanafi scholars of the Indian subcontinent. These are not mere formalities—they serve as a scholarly warranty, confirming that the legal rulings in the book are sound and reliable. Understanding this tradition deepens your appreciation of how authority is constructed in the Hanafi madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the endorsing scholars
List the names of the scholars who provided endorsements, noting their institutions (e.g., Dar al-Ulum Deoband, Mazaahir Uloom Saharanpur).
Look for phrases like 'كتبه العبد الضعيف' and 'الجواب صحيح'.
2
Analyze the endorsement phrases
Observe the standard Arabic/Urdu phrases used: 'الجواب صحيح' (the answer is correct), 'طالعت هذه الضميمة' (I reviewed this appendix), etc.
These phrases indicate verification, not original authorship.
3
Recognize the chain of authority
Note how endorsements from multiple institutions create a network of scholarly consensus (ijmāʿ). The presence of Ashraf ʿAlī Thanwī, Muḥammad Shafīʿ al-Deobandī, and others adds weight.
This practice mirrors the classical ijāza system.
4
Connect to fatwa practice
Understand that a mufti relies on such endorsements to know which works are reliable. This lesson reinforces the hierarchy of sources in Hanafi iftāʾ.
Taṣdīqāt are part of the 'authority weight' assessment.

Commentary
This section is a collection of endorsements (taṣdīqāt) by senior Hanafi scholars, a traditional feature in classical fiqh works to establish scholarly verification and consensus. The endorsements confirm the correctness of the rulings in the book, particularly on the topic of apostasy of one spouse and its effect on marriage. Notable figures include Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, Zafar Ahmad Usmani, Husayn Ahmad Madani, and others. Such endorsements serve as a form of ijāza (scholarly certification) and strengthen the authority of the work within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
تصدیقات (taṣdīqāt): Endorsements or certifications by scholars attesting to the correctness of a book's content.
اکابرین (akābirīn): The great scholars; senior authorities in the field.
الجواب صحيح (al-jawāb ṣaḥīḥ): Literal: 'The answer is correct' – a standard phrase of endorsement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Taṣdīqāt are a classic Hanafi tool for building collective scholarly authority: multiple senior scholars verify a work, ensuring its reliability for future fatwa practice.

Introduction and Front Matter

Endorsements and Maliki Fatawa in Hanafi Iftaa Works
Colophon with endorsements and cross-madhhab note.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of taqrizat (scholarly endorsements) in a Hanafi fiqh work and identify when a Hanafi mufti may utilize fatawa from another school.

Core Idea
Endorsements verify scholarly rigour; Maliki fatawa are a resource for Hanafis only in dire necessity.

This passage concludes 'Al-Hilatul Najijah' with a series of endorsements from prominent Deoband scholars, each affirming 'الجواب صحيح' (The answer is correct). It then adds a note about a separate collection of Maliki fatawa from Medina, explicitly stating that a Hanafi follower may act upon them in severe necessity. Understanding these elements is crucial for a mufti: endorsements establish the reliability of the work, while the cross-madhhab allowance reflects the practical principle of following a stronger or less burdensome ruling under duress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the endorsements and their formula
Read the first part of the passage. Note the names and phrases like 'الجواب صحيح' and 'موافق لجميع ما في الباب'. These are taqrizat: written approvals by scholars, often appended to a book to confirm its correctness and scholarly acceptance.
In Hanafi tradition, such endorsements are not part of the legal content but serve as a chain of scholarly verification.
2
Interpret 'الجواب صحيح' as scholarly approval
Each occurrence of 'الجواب صحيح' means 'The answer is correct.' This is a concise form of taqriz, affirming that the rulings in the book are sound according to the endorsing scholar's view.
These endorsements add weight to the book's authority, especially for later muftis consulting it.
3
Analyze the note on Maliki fatawa and its purpose
The second part explains a separate volume: a collection of fatwas from Medina's Maliki muftis. The key phrase is 'جن پر سخت ضرورت کے موقعہ پر حنفی المسلک کو عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے' — a Hanafi follower is allowed to act upon them in times of severe necessity.
This is a practical application of the Hanafi principle of 'al-ḍarūrah tuqaddar bi qadarihā' (necessity is measured by its extent) and allows following another school when the Hanafi position is too difficult or absent.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Cross-Madhhab Fatwa Collection and Darurah
Introduction to a cross-madhhab fatwa collection and a sample query on missing husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of compiling a collection of fatwas from another madhhab and apply the concept of darurah to a case of a missing husband.

Core Idea
A Hanafi may follow a Maliki fatwa in extreme necessity (darurah) when his own madhhab causes hardship.

This passage introduces a remarkable collection of Maliki fatawa compiled specifically for Hanafis facing dire need. The compiler explains the rationale and provides a sample fatwa concerning a missing husband. This lesson examines the legal mechanism of talfiq across madhhabs in cases of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Collection's Purpose
Read the opening lines to understand why the compiler gathered Maliki fatwas: for Hanafis to act upon in times of severe necessity (sakht zaroorat).
This is a practical tool for muftis, not a doctrinal shift.
2
Understand Talfiq and Darurah
Talfiq is combining rulings from different madhhabs. Here, darurah permits a Hanafi to adopt a Maliki ruling when the Hanafi ruling causes undue hardship.
The Hanafi school generally prohibits talfiq except in necessity.
3
Analyze the Sample Fatwa: Mafqud
The query presents a woman whose husband is missing for years. The Maliki position, based on Mukhtasar Khalil, allows remarriage after four years of waiting. The Hanafi position typically requires much longer (90 years).
Note the three sub-questions: whether a judge's decree is required, and the scenario in non-Muslim lands.
4
Apply the Concept of Darurah
Consider a Hanafi mufti faced with a woman in extreme hardship (e.g., no support, no judge). He may, under the principle of darurah, issue a fatwa based on the Maliki view from this collection.
The mufti must ensure the necessity is genuine and the adopted ruling does not contradict a definitive text.

In this collection, the fatawa of the noble muftis of Medina are assembled, which Hanafis may act upon in times of severe need. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Collection of Maliki fatawa from the fountainheads of fatwa among the scholars of Medina, which we promised in the introduction to append at the end of the treatise along with the number of narrations we took, to facilitate reference to their sources. The query: What says our Maliki masters – may Allah prolong their existence and benefit Muslims with their knowledge – regarding the following questions: (1) A Muslim woman who lost her husband years ago and his situation has not become clear despite much investigation and searching; is it permissible for her, after four years have passed, to observe the iddah of death and then marry another husband? Or must she refer the matter to the ruler or judge or the Muslim community, then investigate the one referred to; if it becomes difficult [to find him], then he rules that she should wait four years; if it does not become clear, she observes the iddah of death as understood from al-Mudawwanah, Mukhtasar Khalil, and its commentary by al-Dardir? How is the ruling? (2) Is the ruling of the judge or the Muslim community regarding the waiting of four years binding? Is that ruling also valid? (3) An Islamic country that has been under the control of disbelievers for a long time, and a Muslim woman from its people has lost her husband there, and there is no Islamic judge to decide rulings according to Sharia laws; what is the way there? In which of the four categories mentioned for the missing person in Mukhtasar Khalil is he considered? And is it valid for the woman there, after four years have passed, to observe the iddah of death and marry? Or is her path only [to remain] unmarried?
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to a collection of Maliki legal opinions (fatawa) compiled for the purpose of providing Hanafi followers a permissible outlet in cases of extreme necessity (sakht zaroorat). The author notes that the collection comes from the muftis of Medina and promises to include it at the end of the treatise with references to original sources. The actual fatwa query addresses a classic case of a missing husband (mafqud). It asks about the permissibility for a woman to remarry after four years of waiting and observing the iddah of death without a judge's involvement, giving precedent from Maliki sources like al-Mudawwanah, Mukhtasar Khalil, and Dardir's commentary. The second part asks about the necessity of a judge's ruling in the waiting period. The third part considers an Islamic land under non-Muslim control with no Islamic judge, asking which of the four categories in Mukhtasar Khalil applies and whether the woman may remarry after four years or must remain unmarried. This fatwa is not a binding ruling but a query for scholarly opinion; the collection as a whole is meant as a resource for Hanafis in need.

Key Terms
مجموعة الفتاوى المالكية (Majmu'at al-Fatawa al-Malikiyyah): A collection of fatwas from Maliki scholars of Medina, compiled for use by Hanafis in dire necessity.
شديدة ضرورة (shadeedah darurah): Extreme necessity that permits a Hanafi to follow a Maliki opinion.
مفقود (mafqud): Missing person – here, a husband whose whereabouts and life status are unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter

The Three Treatises for Oppressed Women: An Overview
Author introduces three treatises addressing women's marital issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three treatises of Al-Hilatul Najizah and explain their purpose in resolving marital issues according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Islam provides legal stratagems (hiyal) for oppressed women; these three treatises collect the Hanafi solutions.

In this lesson, we explore the introduction to a collection of treatises by Ashraf Ali Thanwi, a prominent Hanafi scholar. He addresses the pressing marital problems faced by women and presents a structured set of legal solutions. This overview will help you understand the scope and organization of the work, which is a key resource for muftis dealing with family law issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the misconception
The author begins by addressing a common doubt: that Islam has no solution for oppressed women. Recognize this as the motivation for the work.
The author explicitly rebuts this, showing that Islam does provide relief.
2
Name the three treatises
List the three treatises: Al-Hilatun Najizah (the main work), Al-Mukhtarat (appendix on specific options), and Hukm al-Azwaj (supplement on divorce disputes).
Each treatise targets a different aspect of marital problems.
3
Understand the structure of Al-Hilatun Najizah
Note that this treatise has two parts: one for women not yet married (pre-marriage guidance) and one for married women (post-marriage solutions).
This bipartite division covers prevention and cure.
4
Recognize the role of supplementary treatises
The second and third treatises provide detailed rulings on specific topics: prohibition by affinity, khiyar al-bulugh, khiyar al-kafa'ah, and divorce disputes.
These are essential tools for muftis in complex cases.
5
Appreciate the summary for general understanding
The author notes that the treatises were not easily understood, so a summary was provided. This reflects the mufti's duty to make rulings accessible.
Summaries are common in Hanafi iftaa works for laypeople.

The legal solution for the problems of oppressed women, i.e., Writings for the oppressed. After praise: In the present time, considering the abundance of women's problems and questions, three treatises have been prepared. One is 'al-Hilatun Najizah', in which issues related to marriage are thoroughly and comprehensively collected in which women have general need. In this treatise, a response is also given to the doubt that Islam has not devised any solution for the release of oppressed women. And a solution for release has also been devised for such oppressed women. This treatise has two parts: Part One: For women who have not yet married. Part Two: For women who have already married. The second treatise, which is an appendix to Part Two of the original treatise, named 'al-Mukhtarat', contains detailed rulings on the prohibition of marriage due to relationship (haram musaharat), option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), and option of suitability (khiyar al-kafa'ah). The third treatise, which is a supplement to the original treatise, is 'Hukm al-Azwaj'; it contains detailed rulings on all forms of divorce disagreements between spouses. But these treatises were not easily understood, so a summary of their issues has been written separately in order; in this summary it is briefly explained what course of action is appropriate before marriage, and if marriage has taken place, on which occasions the marriage can be annulled and how.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the work 'Al-Hilatul Najizah' and its companion treatises. It explains the motivation: the abundance of problems faced by women in the present time. The author refutes the misconception that Islam has no solution for oppressed women. He then outlines the structure: the main treatise has two parts (before marriage and after marriage), and two additional treatises ('Al-Mukhtarat' and 'Hukm al-Azwaj') cover specific topics like prohibition by affinity, options of puberty and suitability, and divorce disputes. The author notes that since these treatises were not easily understood by the general public, a summary is also provided. From a Hanafi perspective, this introduction is important as it sets the stage for presenting legal stratagems (hiyal) and rulings that are permissible within the school to resolve marital difficulties. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, was a prominent Hanafi scholar known for his practical fatwas.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): Option of puberty: the right of a minor married by a guardian to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
خیار کفایت (khiyar al-kafa'ah): Option of suitability: the right of a woman or her guardian to annul a marriage if the husband is not equal in status (kufu).
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat musaharah): Prohibition due to affinity: marriage prohibitions arising from relationship through marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, how many treatises are prepared for women's problems?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides multiple legal stratagems for women in marital distress, collected systematically in these three treatises.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Introduction: Purpose and Use of Hanafi Marital Stratagems
Front matter introducing three treatises on women's stratagems

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of the three treatises and identify the conditions for acting on them in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Islam provides lawful stratagems for oppressed women, but they require scholarly oversight and civil law awareness.

This lesson unpacks the introduction to three landmark Hanafi treatises on marital problems. The author, Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains why these works were compiled: to answer the doubt that Islam has no solution for oppressed women and to provide practical stratagems. You will learn the structure of the treatises, the responsibilities of those who use them, and the critical principle that a mufti or scholar must be consulted before any action is taken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's motivation
Read the first part of the passage where the author describes the abundance of women's problems and the doubt that Islam lacks solutions. Note how he refutes this by presenting the treatises.
This motivation is key to understanding the place of hiyal in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Map the three treatises
List the three treatises: al-Ḥīlat an-Nājiza, al-Mukhtārāt, and Ḥukm al-Izwāj. Note their target audiences (unmarried vs. married women) and the specific issues they cover (tafwīḍ, khiyār al-bulūgh, conversion cases).
Treatises cover both preventive measures (before marriage) and remedies (after marriage).
3
Analyze the conditions for application
Identify the two responsibilities the author imposes: (1) consult a reliable scholar, not act independently; (2) verify compliance with civil law through lawyers. Understand why these conditions are necessary for valid fatwa practice.
These conditions reflect the mufti's duty to ensure both shar‘i and legal validity.
4
Extract the Hanafi principle of hiyal
From the fact that these stratagems are permitted, infer the Hanafi acceptance of legal stratagems to achieve lawful ends. Contrast with schools that restrict hiyal.
The treatise itself is a proof of Hanafi practice in this area.
5
Position the source in fatwa hierarchy
Recognize that the treatises are from the fatawa mutakhkhirin period (later Hanafi scholarship). They are not from Zahir al-Riwayah but are widely accepted as mufta bihi due to their practical utility and the author's authority.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin; often relied upon but require scholarly verification.

The shar‘i solution to the problems of oppressed women, i.e., al-Marqūmāt li al-Maẓlūmāt. After praising Allah: In the present time, seeing the abundance of women's problems and questions, three treatises have been prepared. First, al-Ḥīlat an-Nājiza, in which marital issues of common concern to women are collected in a very complete and detailed manner. This treatise also answers the doubt that Islam has not devised any way for the relief of oppressed women, and it also provides a stratagem for the release of such oppressed women. This treatise has two parts: Part One: for women who are not yet married. Part Two: for women who are already married. The second treatise, which is a supplement to Part Two of the original treatise, is called al-Mukhtārāt. It contains detailed rulings on the prohibition of affinity (ḥurmat muṣāharat), the option of puberty (khiyār al-bulūgh), and the option of equality (khiyār al-kafā‘a). The third treatise, which is an appendix to the original, is Ḥukm al-Izwāj, in which detailed and complete rulings are given for all cases of conversion with change of madhhab. However, these treatises were not generally comprehensible, so a summary of their issues has been written separately and arranged. In this summary, it is briefly explained what course is appropriate before marriage, and if marriage has already taken place, in which situations divorce can be annulled and how. For those seeking detail, if they are scholars, they should themselves, and if not, with the help of a scholar, consult the original treatises, which contain the evidence for each issue. It is hoped that this treatise will greatly help oppressed women. But when acting on these issues, two responsibilities lie on those who act: (1) They should not take any action merely by looking at this treatise, relying on their own reading ability. Rather, they should present the actual situation along with this treatise before a reliable scholar and act according to his advice, such that they seek his opinion on every detail and follow it. (2) We are not familiar with the current government's law; so they should inquire from knowledgeable lawyers whether the action is in accordance with or against the law, and then act on their own knowledge and effort. We are not responsible for that. And Allah is the Helper. Upon Him is reliance. Summary: Al-Mujalla an-Nājiza li al-Ḥimla al-‘Ājiza (which has two parts herein). Part One: Regarding delegation of divorce (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq) at the time of marriage (from Hanafi fiqh). Question: The difficulties women face today in India due to the absence of a shar‘i judge are beyond description. The husband oppresses and does not fulfill the wife's rights. He neither provides maintenance nor divorces. Sometimes he abandons wife and children and goes missing, or becomes insane. If a shar‘i judge were present, the solution to these problems would be easy. But the current difficulties are not hidden from anyone. Therefore, it is requested...
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is the introduction (front matter) of the work. The author, Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains the motivation behind compiling three treatises: 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah' (The Successful Stratagem), 'Al-Mukhtarat' (The Selections), and 'Hukm al-Izwaj' (Ruling on Marriage). He notes that many women face marital oppression and the absence of a qadi makes matters worse, leading to doubts that Islam has no solution. The author refutes this by providing detailed legal stratagems. The treatises are divided into sections for unmarried and married women. Importantly, the author emphasizes that these summaries are not to be acted upon without consulting a qualified scholar and also advises checking compatibility with contemporary civil law through lawyers. The first part of the summary deals with delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) at the time of marriage, a key topic in Hanafi fiqh for empowering women.

Key Terms
الحیلۃ الناجزہ (al-Ḥīlat an-Nājiza): The title of the first treatise, meaning 'The Successful Stratagem', containing marital solutions for women.
تفویض طلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): Delegation of divorce, where the husband gives his wife the authority to divorce herself under certain conditions.
خیار بلوغ (khiyār al-bulūgh): Option of puberty: the right of a minor married by a guardian to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
حرمت مصاہرت (ḥurmat muṣāharat): Prohibition of affinity: marital relationships that create permanent prohibition of marriage between certain relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, what is the main purpose of the treatise 'Al-Hilat an-Najizah'?
A) To provide a complete guide for Islamic inheritance.
B) To answer the doubt that Islam has no solution for oppressed women and to provide legal stratagems.
C) To explain the differences between Hanafi and Shafi'i fiqh.
D) To discuss the rules of prayer and fasting.

Key Takeaway
These treatises are a practical application of Hanafi hiyal, but fatwa practice demands that no action be taken without scholarly consultation and civil law awareness.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Authority of Scholarly Endorsements in Fatwa Works
Conclusion with reaffirmation, summary, and endorsements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of scholarly endorsements (taṣdīqāt) in authenticating a Hanafi fatwa work and identify the practical obligations they impose on the mufti and the mustafti.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements are testimony to a work's reliability and bind practitioners to follow its conditions.

This passage concludes the treatise Hīla Nājiza with a reaffirmation of a ruling on apostasy and marriage, a summary of three juristic works, and critical endorsements. For the Hanafi mufti, such endorsements are not merely ceremonial—they serve as a verification mechanism, ensuring that the work's contents are reliable and that its conditions must be strictly observed. This lesson examines how endorsements function as a source of authority in the iftā’ tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reaffirmed ruling
Locate the ruling on apostasy: she remains married but intercourse is prohibited until renewal of faith and marriage. This reinforces the Hanafi position that apostasy suspends but does not dissolve the marriage.
This ruling is stated before the endorsements, showing the author's concluding emphasis.
2
Analyze the endorsement's content
Read al-Tahānavī's endorsement: he praises the treatise as 'unique', 'beneficial', and commends the author's exhaustive effort. Note his use of superlatives and prayer for acceptance.
Such language signals strong approval and recommends the work to the community.
3
Extract practical requirements
The passage ends with a request: adhere strictly to the conditions (quyūd wa shurūṭ) recorded, avoid following whims under the guise of necessity, and muftis should study the work carefully.
This shows that endorsements carry an ethical obligation on the part of practitioners.
4
Connect to iftā’ methodology
Reflect on how endorsements function as a form of tazkiyah (validation) in the Hanafi tradition. A mufti often relies on works that have been vetted by recognized scholars.
This ensures consistency and trustworthiness in fatwa issuance.

Praise be to Allah, and sufficient peace be upon His chosen servants. Thereafter, I have perused this unique treatise, and my eyes have been delighted by the lights of these beneficial pearls, so I found it singular in this chapter and a unique rose taken from the depth of the sea. Among them: the sweetness of every truth dead from death with every false word; among them: the whiteness of every black heart from the blackness of every eye. Allah and our master have exhausted in verification and exposition, and exerted effort in facilitation and ease for the oppressed community. May Allah make this effort thanked and this work accepted and blessed. And may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family and all his companions. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After praise and salutations, it is reported that the great necessity of this beneficial treatise is apparent, and its comprehensive, preventive, and immensely useful nature is not in need of explanation. Even a cursory viewer involuntarily says: 'From difference to existence, wherever I look, a gesture pulls the skirt of the heart: this is the place.' In reality, the solution to this important problem of the deceased community required a person like His Holiness, who is a gathering of perfections. The extent of solitary reflection and exertion that you have devoted to its research and composition over a long period can only be appreciated by those who were blessed with presence during the time of composition. His Holiness repeatedly stated that no work in a lifetime has caused such hardship. May Allah the Exalted keep the shade of mercy of His Holiness (may his blessings endure) over our heads, constantly and eternally, Amen, then Amen. Now, from the people of need, only this much request: the restrictions and conditions recorded in this treatise are extremely necessary; keep them well in mind at the time of practice and fully observe them. Be not one who, under the pretext of necessity, follows the whims of the soul. Also, request the service of the fatwa-granting scholars for grace and solicitation.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage concludes the book with a summary of its contents and scholarly endorsements. It begins with a reaffirmation of the ruling regarding a woman who has apostatized: she remains under her husband's possession and cannot marry another, but sexual relations are prohibited until she renews Islam and marriage. This underscores the Hanafi position that apostasy does not automatically dissolve the marriage but suspends its consummation. The text then transitions to the summary of three juristic treatises—Hīla Nājiza, al-Mukhtārāt, and Tatimmatu Hukmi al-Azwāj—indicating that the current work is a composite of these. The following endorsements (taṣdīqāt) from scholars, notably Zafar Ahmad al-Tahānavī, testify to the treatise's uniqueness and utility. The scholar praises the author's exhaustive efforts in research and exposition, emphasizing that the work was produced with great hardship to facilitate the Muslim community. The passage ends with an earnest request to muftis and practitioners to adhere strictly to the conditions and restrictions laid out in the treatise, warning against laxity under the guise of necessity. This section serves as a testament to the book's authenticity and the author's meticulous scholarship, inviting trust and careful application.

Key Terms
حیلہ ناجزہ (Hīla Nājiza): A Hanafi legal stratagem designed to resolve marital disputes without violating Sharia, specifically addressing cases where a wife cannot obtain divorce or maintenance.
تصدیق (taṣdīq): An endorsement or verification by a recognized scholar attesting to the reliability and correctness of a work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the endorsements (taṣdīqāt) included in this section?
A) To prove the author's lineage and family background.
B) To authenticate the treatise and verify its usefulness and scholarly merit.
C) To list all the books the author has written.
D) To provide a legal ruling on a new issue.

Key Takeaway
Endorsements authenticate a work; the mufti and layperson must adhere strictly to the conditions laid out in a verified treatise.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Function of Taqriz in Hanafi Fatwa Collections
Endorsements from scholars praising the book and its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of a taqriz in a Hanafi fatwa collection and identify how it establishes the authority and practical importance of the work.

Core Idea
Taqriz authenticates a fatwa collection and signals that its conditions are binding for practice.

This passage presents endorsements from two scholars of the Hilat al-Najizah. These taqriz are not mere praise; they serve to assure the reader that the book's rulings are reliable and that its stated conditions must be strictly followed. Understanding the role of taqriz is part of the mufti's training in evaluating sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authors of the taqriz
Note the names and positions of the endorsers (Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi, Siraj Ahmad, 'Abd al-Karim). Their stature gives weight to the endorsement.
They are associated with Khanqah Imdadiyya and Madrasa Mazahir al-Ulum.
2
Extract the core claims of each taqriz
What do they say about the necessity of the book, the effort of the author, and the importance of following the conditions?
Both stress that the conditions in the book are essential and must not be neglected.
3
Analyze the role of the endorsements in the iftaa process
How do these taqriz support a mufti who uses this book? They confirm that the fatwas are sound and that the school's rules have been applied.
One endorsement explicitly mentions that even though the author's fatwa does not need verification, they still attest to it.

Upon the oppressed nation and ease - may God make this effort accepted and this work blessed and approved, and may God bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions altogether. Written by his pen, the humblest of servants and the most insignificant of slaves, Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi, may God cover him with poverty and pleasure. 26 Dhu al-Hijjah, year. In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After praise and salutation, it is evident that this treatise is extremely necessary, and its comprehensive, preventing, and immensely beneficial nature need not be stated. Even a cursory glance will spontaneously say... In reality, the solution to this important problem of the deceased community required a person like His Holiness, who is a collection of perfections. The deep contemplation and prolonged effort he devoted to its investigation and authorship can only be appreciated by those who had the fortune of being present during its compilation. His Holiness repeatedly stated that he had never worked so hard in his life on any task. May God keep the shadow of His Holiness's mercy over our heads, Amen, then Amen. Now, the only request to those in need is that the restrictions and conditions recorded in this treatise are extremely necessary; at the time of practice, keep them well in view and strictly adhere to them, and do not deviate due to pretext of dire need and following desire. Also, I request the honorable scholars of fatwa that they make it necessary to keep all conditions well in view at the time of giving fatwa. And He is the Guide to good and the Protector from all harm. The petitioner, Siraj Ahmad, may God forgive him. The lowest of servants, the most insignificant of attendants, 'Abd al-Karim, may God pardon him. From Khanqah Imdadiyya, Thana Bhawan, 26 Ramadan, blessed, 26 Ramadan, blessed, Sadr. Teacher at Khanqah Imdadiyya, Pehar. From Madrasa Mazahir al-Ulum, Saharanpur. In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, praising and sending blessings and peace. After this, we studied this al-Fatwa al-Jabi'iyya al-Najiza carefully and thoroughly for about a month and a half, repeatedly. We believe that in this time, a jurist like His Holiness Hakim al-Ummat, Majd al-Millat, Maulana Thanwi, who has complete mastery of apparent and inner sciences and is well aware of contemporary conditions and present problems, certainly has the right to adopt for fatwa the school of another imam, because at times of dire necessity, adopting another imam's school is also a ruling of Hanafi fiqh. Therefore, although His Holiness's fatwa is not in need of verification and correction from the likes of us, but for the sake of good and precaution, we acquire the honor of verifying and correcting these issues.

This passage contains the taqriz (endorsements) of Al-Hilat al-Najizah by two scholars: Zafar Ahmad al-Thanawi (possibly a relative or student) and Siraj Ahmad and 'Abd al-Karim. The first endorsement highlights the necessity of the work and the immense effort the author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, put into it. It stresses that the conditions mentioned in the book are essential and must be followed carefully. The second endorsement, from 'Abd al-Karim, confirms the book's thoroughness and notes that adopting another imam's school in times of necessity is a valid Hanafi principle. This front matter establishes the authority and practical importance of the book.

فتوى الجبيلة الناجزہ (al-Fatwa al-Jabi'iyya al-Najiza): The title of the book, meaning 'The Fruitful Fatwa that Serves the Need'

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Adopting Another Madhhab in Times of Necessity: A Hanafi Iftaa Principle
Endorsement affirming the right to adopt another madhhab in necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that permits adopting another madhhab for fatwa in times of dire necessity and identify its conditions as mentioned in the endorsement.

Core Idea
In dire necessity, a Hanafi mufti may adopt another madhhab's ruling because that itself is a ruling of the Hanafi school.

The second endorsement of al-Hilat al-Najizah explicitly states that Ashraf Ali Thanwi, due to his expertise and the pressing needs of the time, has the right to adopt for fatwa the school of another imam. This is not a departure from Hanafism but an application of its own internal principle. This lesson unpacks that principle and its significance for iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Locate the statement of the principle
Find the sentence: 'بوقت شديده دوسرے اماموں کے مذہب کو اختیار کرنا بھی فقہ حنفی کا ایک حکم ہے.' This is the core claim.
2
Identify the justification
The endorser says that because the author is a 'فقیہ ... مہارت تامہ' and 'احوال زمانہ ومشکلات حاضرہ سے بخوبی واقف', he has the right to adopt other madhhab. Why is being a qualified jurist a condition?
The mufti must have enough knowledge to correctly apply the other madhhab's ruling.
3
Determine the scope of the principle
Is this principle absolute or qualified? The phrase 'بوقت شديده' indicates it is for dire necessity. Also, the first endorsement stresses that the book's own conditions must still be followed, implying that even when adopting another madhhab, one must adhere to the conditions of that ruling.
Necessity does not mean abandoning conditions; it means selecting a valid alternative from another school.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi iftaa methodology
This principle is part of talfiq (combining rulings) or takhayyur (selection). It is allowed under strict limitations to alleviate hardship. Later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Abidin elaborate on this.
This is not unrestricted eclecticism.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Endorsements and Temporal Necessity in Hanafi Fatwa Practice
Endorsements and certifications from prominent scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how scholar endorsements (taqriz) certify a work for fatwa and how the principle of temporal necessity (ḍarūriyāt waqtiyya) justifies adapting rulings, using the missing husband (mafqood) case as an example.

Core Idea
Scholar endorsements confirm that a work's solutions are rooted in Hanafi tradition and suitable for current needs, especially when temporal necessity demands adaptation.

This passage contains endorsements from leading scholars of Mazahir Uloom and Darul Uloom Deoband for Al-Hilat al-Najizah. They certify its correctness and emphasize that in the current circumstances, its solutions are necessary and must be adopted. They specifically invoke the Hanafi principle of temporal necessity (ḍarūriyāt waqtiyya) applied to cases like the missing husband (mafqood). This lesson explores the role of such endorsements in fatwa practice and the crucial concept of necessity-based legal adaptation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type
This is front matter (taqriz/taṣdīq) – endorsements from senior scholars that certify the work.
Endorsements are not independent fatwas but affirm the reliability of the book's content.
2
Recognize the scholars' authority
The scholars come from Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur and Darul Uloom Deoband, institutions renowned for Hanafi scholarship. Their names and titles (e.g., Shaykh al-Fiqh wa al-Adab) indicate seniority.
The authority of the endorsers lends weight to the certification.
3
Understand the purpose of the endorsement
The scholars state they have examined the book and found it correct. They urge scholars to adopt its solutions and give fatwa accordingly. This is a recommendation, not a binding decree.
The phrase 'no solution other than this seems possible' highlights the perceived necessity.
4
Extract the key legal concept
The scholars mention 'ḍarūriyāt waqtiyya' (temporal necessities) as the basis for the solutions, citing earlier Hanafi jurists who used this principle for the mafqood case.
This shows the Hanafi tradition of ijtihad within the madhhab to address contemporary hardships.
5
Connect to the mafqood case
The missing husband problem is a classic scenario where necessity permits relaxation of standard waiting period rules. The endorsements confirm that the book's solutions follow this precedent.
Understanding the mafqood case helps illustrate how temporal necessity operates in practice.

وانا العبد المذنب ظفر احمد عفا الله عنه ۲۹ - رمضان ساده
His Holiness (may his shadow remain high) has worked with such research, precision, and caution in this fatwa that cannot be expressed. We raise our hands in prayer from the core of our heart to the Majesty of Allah, the Blessed, that He keep His Holiness safe on the path of the guides with all these effusions and blessings for a long time, Amin. We believe that the beautiful efforts of His Holiness will be thanked by the merciful nation until the Day of Resurrection. May Allah give the best reward from us and all Muslims. Written by: 'Abd al-Latif, Nazim Madrasa Band 'Abd al-Rahman, forgiven; Muhammad Zakariyya Kandhlawi, Muhammad As'ad Allah, forgive him; Muhammad Mazahir Uluum (first teacher, teacher of Madrasa Mazahir Uluum... ... We have thoroughly examined the treatise (Al-Hilat al-Najizah li al-Hilat al-'Ajizah). Indeed, in our current circumstances and existing conditions, no solution other than this seems possible: that the scholars of the negative (?) madhhab adopt the mentioned issues of this treatise as practiced and give fatwa upon it. Even in past centuries, Hanafi scholars adopted this approach in the matter of the missing husband and similar issues due to temporal necessities. The great efforts and utmost exertion of the revered author (may his blessings endure) and his assistants in the above-mentioned issues are, without doubt and unquestionably, worthy of thousands of thanks and praise. May Allah the Exalted grant them the best reward in both worlds. Amin. Signed: al-Sa'id: ... Muhammad Tayyib, ..., Muhammad Shafi', ..., etc. Certifications related to the selection: We examined the supplement (al-timmah) and found it correct. Signed: Ashraf 'Ali (forgiven), ... Muhammad Shafi', ... Siraj Ahmad, ... Zafar Ahmad (forgiven). Dated 29 Ramadan.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage consists of endorsements (taqrizat) from leading scholars of Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur and Darul Uloom Deoband, certifying the correctness and necessity of the legal solutions presented in Al-Hilat al-Najizah. The scholars emphasize that in the present circumstances, there is no alternative but to adopt the solutions provided in this work and issue fatwa based on it. They explicitly invoke the precedent of earlier Hanafi jurists who, in the case of the missing husband (mafqood) and similar issues, adapted rulings based on temporal needs (darurat waqtiyya). This highlights the Hanafi tradition of ijtihad within the madhhab to address contemporary problems without abandoning the foundational principles. The endorsements conclude with prayers and signatures, affirming the book's authority and acceptance within the scholarly community.

Key Terms
تقرير / تصديق (taqrīr / taṣdīq): Endorsement or certification by a scholar attesting to the correctness and reliability of a work and its contents.
مسئله مفقود (mas'alah mafqūd): The legal problem of a missing husband whose whereabouts are unknown and whose return is not expected, affecting the wife's ability to remarry.
ضروریات وقتیہ (ḍarūriyāt waqtiyya): Temporal necessities or urgent circumstances that require a departure from the default ruling to prevent hardship, guiding legal accommodation in changing times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A new revelation from Allah
B) The principle of temporal necessities (ḍarūriyāt waqtiyya)
C) A decision by a caliph
D) The personal opinion of the author of Al-Hilat al-Najizah

Key Takeaway
Scholar endorsements and the principle of temporal necessity work together to allow the adaptation of Hanafi rulings to meet contemporary needs, as exemplified by the mafqood case.

The Role of Scholarly Endorsements in Hanafi Scholarship
Scholarly endorsements from three madrasas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of scholarly endorsements (tasdiqat) and explain their role in establishing the reliability of a Hanafi text.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements (tasdiqat) are the collective stamp of approval from respected authorities, confirming a text's correctness and mufta bihi status.

This page from Thanwi's compilation is not a ruling but a record of endorsements. Though it may seem like mere formality, these tasdiqat are crucial in the Hanafi tradition for verifying that a work is reliable for fatwa. Understanding their function helps you navigate later sources with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the page type
Identify that this is a tasdiqat page, not a legal discussion or fatwa. It is a paratextual element documenting scholarly approval.
2
Identify the endorsing scholars and institutions
Look at the names of madrasas and individual scholars mentioned: Imdad al-Ulum Thana Bhawan, Darul Uloom Deoband, Mazahir Uloom Saharanpur, and specific figures like Ashraf Ali, Abd al-Karim, Muhammad Shafi, etc.
These are reputable institutions in the South Asian Hanafi tradition.
3
Understand the approval phrases
Note the repeated phrase 'الجواب صحيح' (the answer is correct). This indicates that the scholars have reviewed the book's contents and found them sound for fatwa.
Similar phrases include 'صحيح' and 'مصيب'.
4
Appreciate the historical practice
Tasdiqat serve as a form of scholarly verification, akin to ijma sukuti (silent consensus) or at least collective endorsement, reinforcing the text's authority.
This practice is common in later Hanafi works, especially those compiled for muftis.

Introduction and Front Matter

Scholarly Endorsements and Their Role in Hanafi Iftaa
Book completion announcement and endorsements from Delhi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and function of scholarly endorsements (tasdiqat) in the Hanafi tradition and identify how they contribute to the authority of a fatwa compilation.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements authenticate a work but do not change its legal content — they are meta-textual seals of approval.

This lesson examines the concluding section of Al-Hilat al-Najizah, where the author announces the completion of his work and presents endorsements from scholars of Delhi. While these endorsements are not part of the legal rulings themselves, they play a crucial role in establishing the credibility and reliability of the book within the Hanafi scholarly tradition. Understanding the function of tasdiqat helps a student of iftaa appreciate how scholarly authority is conferred and maintained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components
Read the passage and separate it into three parts: (a) continuation of a legal discussion, (b) completion note, (c) endorsements.
2
Differentiate legal argument from meta-text
Note that the endorsements do not contain legal rulings but are meta-commentary validating the author and his work.
Endorsements are not sources of fiqh; they are scholarly recommendations.
3
Analyze the endorsing scholars
List the names and the institution (Madrasa Islamiya Fatehpuri, Delhi) of the scholars who endorsed the book.
These are teachers, indicating institutional backing.
4
Understand the purpose of endorsements
Recognize that endorsements serve to increase trust among the Muslim community and to show that the book aligns with the accepted positions of the Hanafi school.
Endorsements are a form of communal validation.
5
Reflect on authority hierarchy
Consider how endorsements from multiple scholars strengthen the authority of the book, but the content itself is based on earlier reliable sources (zahir al-riwayah, etc.).
Endorsements do not override the hierarchy of texts; they confirm correct application.

Of the three types, the first type, that they make him a guardian and then he comes as a judge, is very far from our region, and the second type is insufficient as mentioned, and the third type 'we make the non-Muslim guardian with the consent of the Muslims' is possible, but for years continuous effort has been ongoing, but still from the first day, and if God Almighty grants success, then even then the solution is not possible without adopting the Maliki school's opinion, because handing over to the judge does not solve the problem, as was already mentioned in the previous letter.
First, opposing the author of Hidayah and other great scholars is difficult, especially when the reason for their opinion, i.e., the fear of the common people falling into difficulty, is increasing nowadays, as is observed.
Second, in the case of a missing person, appointing a third religious arbitrator is not possible because the consent of both parties is a condition, and the consent of the missing person cannot be obtained; therefore, a fatwa appointing an arbitrator cannot be given. Only God knows best, and His knowledge is most perfect and most wise.

Endorsements of the scholars of Delhi.
From Madrasa Islamiya Fatehpuri, praising and blessing. Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of Al-Hilat al-Najizah. It contains two parts: a brief continuation of a previous discussion regarding the practical difficulties of appointing a judge or arbitrator in certain cases, and then the formal completion note and endorsements. The discussion reiterates the challenge of implementing certain legal stratagems without adopting the Maliki school's opinion. The completion note announces that the book is finished. This is followed by endorsements from several scholars of Madrasa Islamiya Fatehpuri, Delhi, who authenticate the work and praise its author, Hakim al-Ummah Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi. These endorsements serve as a stamp of approval to the content of the book, confirming its religious and scholarly value. For students of Hanafi usul al-iftaa, this demonstrates the importance of scholarly validation in the tradition.

Key Terms
تصدیقات (tasdiqat): Endorsements or certifications by scholars verifying the correctness and usefulness of the book.
