Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Necessity and Adopting Other Imams' Rulings
Scholarly endorsements affirming the permissibility of adopting other imams' rulings under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that necessity (darurah) permits adopting another imam's ruling or a weak position, and identify the conditions required for such departure.

Core Idea
Necessity can make a weak or abandoned position the mufta bih — but only with thorough investigation and genuine public need.

This passage contains endorsements (taqriz) from several scholars praising the work 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah'. The endorsers highlight the core methodology: in response to severe difficulties faced by Muslims in India, the author has collected Hanafi fiqh issues where adherence to the dominant position has become practically impossible. To remove these hardships, it is permissible to give fatwa according to the sayings of other imams or according to weak or abandoned positions within the Hanafi school. However, this is not arbitrary; it must be based on genuine necessity (darurah) that affects the general populace, and must involve thorough verification (tahqiq wa tanqih) and fulfillment of all necessary conditions. This passage illustrates a key principle of rasm al-mufti: the conditions under which a mufti may depart from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context and problem
Read the endorsements and note what practical issue the treatise addresses. The scholars mention 'difficulties encountered in India' and 'hardships of this time.'
The problem is widespread difficulty in practicing the standard Hanafi rulings.
2
Extract the permission principle
Find the sentence that states the permissibility: 'Due to necessities, it is permissible to give fatwa according to the saying of another imam or to make a weak and abandoned saying mufta bih.'
This is the core ruling endorsed by the scholars.
3
Note the conditions and limitations
Identify the conditions mentioned: necessity must be real, not restricted to an individual, and must involve thorough investigation and necessary conditions. The passage says 'with complete investigation and purification and necessary conditions.'
The conditions prevent arbitrary departure from the madhhab.
4
Understand the implications for ifta practice
Consider how this principle applies today. A mufti facing a novel situation or widespread hardship must assess whether darurah exists, then if necessary, adopt a different opinion, but only after careful research and ensuring the adopted ruling is valid and meets all conditions.
This is a key element of rasm al-mufti: the mufti's role in balancing adherence to the madhhab with the needs of the community.

By letter read: The difficulties encountered in India due to the issues of this treatise are clearer than the sun. Due to necessities, it is permissible to give fatwa according to the saying of another imam or to make a weak and abandoned saying mufta bih. And that necessity is not restricted to a particular person. Rather it is important for the people of the time, and the necessity may be limited to worldly necessities or may not be, while in many cases it also leads to religion. In such cases, exceeding mere permissibility is not surprising. Accordingly, in the mentioned treatise, those issues of Hanafi fiqh in which difficulty in practice arises due to the hardships of this time are all collected. And for the sake of repelling necessity, fatwa is given on the sayings of other imams with complete investigation and purification and necessary conditions. That the treatise is comprehensive and prevents (deficiencies) and does not miss any aspect or corner—that alone was sufficient to indicate the attribution of the author (may Allah prolong him with virtue). But after seeing the treatise, its conviction is achieved in a research-based manner. Then my confirmation, or even anyone's confirmation, cannot create any beauty in the said treatise. However, incidentally, speech and also from some situation came that this humble person considers this companionship of his name as a means of salvation in the hereafter. Therefore, I present these lines. Ittifaq al-Rahman Kandhlawi, Madrasa Fathpuri Delhi.
From Madrasa Abd al-Rabb Delhi. 28 Rabi' al-Awwal, Tuesday, 35 AH.
After that! This servant and other teachers of Madrasa Mawlawi Abd al-Rabb (late) Delhi carefully examined the collection of treatises al-Hilat al-Najizah etc. Indeed, His Holiness (may his shadow be prolonged) has dealt with such research and precision in these fatwas that we cannot fully praise it. Certainly, looking at the present condition in India, there is no other way except that scholars should give fatwas according to this treatise. And His Holiness has completely organized a great trial. And he has the right that, considering necessities, he may adopt the madhhab of another imam. May Allah reward them with the best reward.
Muhammad Shafi' Deobandi, teacher of Mahbub al-Ilahi (forgiven), Deobandi teacher, in Dar al-Rabbiyy? Delhi.

Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage comprises endorsements (taqriz) from several scholars praising the book 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah' by Ashraf Ali Thanwi. The endorsements highlight the core methodology of the work: in response to the severe difficulties (mashaqq) faced by Muslims in India, the author has compiled Hanafi fiqh rulings where adherence to the dominant position has become practically insurmountable. To remove these hardships, the fatwa is given according to the sayings of other imams (e.g., Imam Abu Yusuf or Imam Muhammad, or even non-Hanafi imams) or according to weak or abandoned positions within the Hanafi school. The endorsements emphasize that this is permissible only when necessity (darurah) exists, and the necessity is not restricted to a particular individual but affects the general populace. Furthermore, the necessity is not limited to worldly matters; it can extend to religious concerns. The scholars approving the work stress that the author has conducted thorough verification (tahqiq wa tanqih) and fulfilled all necessary conditions. They consider the book a timely solution to prevent a great trial (fitnah) and confidently state that scholars should follow its guidance. This passage demonstrates the principles of rasm al-mufti regarding talfiq and adopting other imams' opinions under necessity.

Key Terms
ضرورت (darurah): Necessity that makes permissible departure from the standard Hanafi position (e.g., adopting another imam's ruling) to remove hardship.
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The ruling that is relied upon for giving fatwa; here it can be a weak or abandoned saying if necessity demands.
تحقیق وتنقیح (tahqiq wa tanqih): Thorough investigation and purification (of the legal ruling) to ensure its validity and applicability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the endorsements, what condition must be present for a mufti to adopt a weak or abandoned saying as mufta bih?
A) The weaker saying must be from Imam Abu Hanifa only
B) Necessity must be present and must be restricted to a specific person
C) Necessity must be genuine and general, and the mufti must conduct thorough investigation
D) Only when the ruler commands it

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, genuine necessity can justify adopting a weak or non-Hanafi ruling as mufta bih, but only after thorough investigation and fulfillment of strict conditions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Scholarly Endorsements (Taqrizat) in the Hanafi Tradition
Endorsements from Hanafi scholars certifying the book's utility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of taqrizat in Hanafi fatwa practice and explain how the endorsements of scholars like Mufti Muhammad Shafi Deobandi validate Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements establish a work’s reliability and mufta bihi status – a critical gatekeeping mechanism in the Hanafi iftaa tradition.

In the Hanafi tradition, a scholarly work does not stand alone—especially one on fatwa methodology. Taqrizat, or endorsements from established scholars, serve as a crucial layer of verification. This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah contains endorsements from several eminent Deobandi scholars, certifying the book's correctness and utility. Understanding this process is essential for any mufti-in-training: it reveals how authority is built and maintained in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the endorsers and their stature
List the scholars mentioned in the passage (Mufti Muhammad Shafi Deobandi, Rashid Ahmad, Abdur Rahman, Muhammad Qasimi, Sayyid Tahir Husain, Akhtar Shah) and note their credentials (teachers at Darul Uloom Deoband, madrasa heads).
These scholars were recognized authorities in the Indian Hanafi tradition.
2
Understand the purpose of their endorsements
The endorsements are not fatwas but certificates of reliability. They confirm the work adheres to Hanafi principles and is beneficial for contemporary problems.
Phrases like 'absolutely correct and sound' and 'life-giving' indicate approval, not legal ruling.
3
Apply the lesson to iftaa practice
Discuss how a mufti today would weigh such endorsements when deciding whether to use a work. The endorsements transform a personal collection into an authoritative reference.
This mirrors the Hanafi hierarchy: zahir al-riwayah > nawadir > fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage contains endorsements (taqrizat) from several eminent scholars of the Indian subcontinent, including Mufti Muhammad Shafi Deobandi, Rashid Ahmad, Abdur Rahman, Muhammad Qasimi, Sayyid Tahir Husain, Akhtar Shah, and others, praising the book 'Al-Hilatul Najijah' (or 'Al-Hilatul Aajizah') by Ashraf Ali Thanwi. They commend the work for addressing contemporary marital issues through permissible legal stratagems (hila shar'iyyah) and for providing relief to oppressed women. The endorsements affirm the book's correctness and its importance for Muslim communities facing modern challenges. The first endorsement highlights the necessity of adopting a different madhhab when required by necessity. The second endorsement emphasizes the book's timely benefit and life-giving effect. The third group endorsement underscores the value of the book for muftis and scholars. The final endorsement (incomplete) mentions the book's utility in judiciary matters. These taqrizat serve as scholarly certifications, establishing the work's credibility in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
الحیلۃ الناجزہ (al-hilat al-najizah): The title of the book, meaning 'the successful stratagem' or 'the effective device', referring to legal stratagems derived from Hanafi fiqh to resolve marital disputes.
تصدیقات (tasdiqat): Endorsements or certifications by scholars confirming the correctness and reliability of the book's contents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) To request a fatwa

Key Takeaway
Endorsements from established scholars are essential for a fatwa work to gain acceptance as mufta bihi in the Hanafi tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Author's Preface: Scope and Purpose of Al-Hilat al-Najizah
Author's preface praising the book's judicial utility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and scope of the risala 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah' and distinguish between the domains of qada and ifta in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Core Idea
This risala provides lawful stratagems for marital disputes when a qualified qadi is absent.

This lesson introduces the author's preface to 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah li al-Hilat al-Ajizah'. Though a brief benediction and praise, the preface clarifies that the book addresses mas'il related to qada (judicial rulings), not general fatwa. Understanding the distinction between qada (binding court decisions) and ifta (advisory opinions) is essential for correctly using this work, which offers legal stratagems (hiyal) for women trapped in difficult marriages when no proper Islamic court is available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genre and function
This is an author's preface (dibajah). Prefaces set the context, purpose, and scope of a book. Note the humility formula 'banda' (the servant) and the praise.
Prefaces often contain key clues about the intended audience and legal methodology.
2
Extract the scope of the book
The author says the book deals with 'masa'il jin ka ta'alluq qada se hai' (issues related to judicial rulings). This tells us the book is about problems that would normally be resolved by a qadi but provides alternative solutions when a qadi is unavailable.
Qada is binding; ifta is non-binding advice. The preface emphasizes qada, not general ifta.
3
Recognize the key term: hila
The title uses 'al-Hilat' (stratagem). In Hanafi fiqh, hila is a lawful device to achieve a permissible end without violating Shari'a. The preface calls the book 'life-giving' and 'correct guidance', indicating the stratagems are legitimate and necessary.
Hila is not trickery but a legitimate juristic tool, especially in dire situations.
4
Connect to the audience and purpose
The preface praises each part as 'muhiyyah' (life-giving) and refers to 'helpless women' (al-ajizah). This suggests the book is meant for scholars and muftis who need to resolve marital disputes of women in distress, especially where no qadi shar'i is present.
The audience is likely judges, muftis, and advanced students of fiqh.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم حامدا ومصلیا اما بعد بنده نے حضرت حکیم الامت مسجد و الملہ حضرت مولانا اشرف علی صاحب زید مجدہم کی کتاب الحیلۃ الناجزہ للحیلۃ العاجزہ کا من و مینوں کے بغور تامل مطالعہ کیا ۔ در حقیقت کتاب اُن مسائل میں کہ جن کا تعلق قضاء سے ہے نہایت کار آمد اور مفید ہے اور اس کا ہر جز محیہ اور ہر مشکلہ مسلمانوں کے لیے مشکل ہدایت ہے اس کتاب سے وہ تمام

Indeed, the book is extremely useful and beneficial in those matters that pertain to qada (judicial rulings). Every part of it is life-giving, and every difficult issue is a correct guidance for Muslims. Through this book, all those...
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This is the author's own introduction to his risala 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah li al-Hilat al-Ajizah' (The Effective Stratagem for the Helpless Woman). The passage is a preface (dibajah) in which the author, Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, declares that he has carefully examined his own work. He then praises the book, emphasizing that it addresses legal matters related to qada (judicial proceedings). The phrase 'har juzz muhiyyah' (every part is life-giving) indicates that the risala provides practical solutions for Muslims, especially women, in difficult marital situations. The author's use of 'بنده' (this servant) is a standard expression of humility. This introduction sets the stage for the legal stratagems (hiyal) that will follow, all aimed at resolving disputes when a qualified qadi shar'i is unavailable.

Key Terms
الحیلۃ الناجزہ (al-Hilat al-Najizah): The effective or immediate stratagem (legal device) intended to resolve a helpless woman's marital predicament.
قضاء (qada): Judicial rulings and court proceedings; matters that fall under the jurisdiction of a qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, what type of issues does the book primarily address?
A) Matters of worship (ibadat)
B) Matters related to judicial rulings (qada)
C) Matters of inheritance (faraid)
D) Matters of business transactions (buyu)

Key Takeaway
The preface establishes that 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah' is a specialized work providing lawful stratagems for marital disputes that fall under the domain of qada, especially when a qualified Islamic judge is unavailable.
